Zakat on Cows Between 40 and 60: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for the excess between 40 and 60 cows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on zakat for cows between 40 and 60, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to determine zakat liability for any number in that range.

Core Idea
The excess between 40 and 60 cows triggers a disagreement: Abu Hanifa requires proportional zakat; the Sahibayn require none until 60.

In this lesson, we examine one of the classical intra-Hanafi disputes regarding the zakat on cows. The issue focuses on the interval numbers (al-waqs) between the fixed nisabs of 40 and 60. Understanding this ikhtilaf not only clarifies the rulings but also illustrates how different textual evidence is weighed within the school. By the end, you will be able to calculate zakat under each view and understand which position is typically relied upon in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State precisely what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule for cows between 40 and 60.
Abu Hanifa: wajib proportional to the increase (e.g., 1/40 musinnah per extra cow). Sahibayn: no zakat until the total reaches 60.
2
Examine the proofs
Locate the dalil for each position. Abu Hanifa relies on the principle of proportional calculation (athar from Makhul: 'ما زاد فبالحساب'). The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet said there is no zakat on al-awqas.
The hadith is quoted in the source: 'لا تأخذ من ذلك شيئا' (do not take anything from that).
3
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
Calculate zakat for a specific number between 40 and 60 (e.g., 50 cows) under each view. This shows the practical difference.
Under Abu Hanifa: for 50 cows (40 + 10 extra), zakat = 10 × 1/40 musinnah = 1/4 musinnah. Under Sahibayn: no zakat because 50 < 60.
4
Recognize the mufta bihi
Note that later Hanafi fatwa often adopts the Sahibayn's position as the cautious view, but this text does not explicitly settle it.
Check later sources like al-Hidayah or al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya for the final tarjih.

Source Text

[۴۶۴] (۲) فاذا زادت على الاربعين وجب فى الزيادة بقدر ذلك الى ستين عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله ففى الواحدة ربع عشر مسنة و في الاثنين نصف عشر مسنة و فى الثلاثة ثلثة ارباع عشر مسنة [۴۶۵](۳) وقال ابو يوسف و محمد لا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ ستين فيكون فيها تبيعان او تبیعتان
ات ربع عشر : دسویں حصہ کی چوتھائی یعنی چالیسواں حصہ، نصف عشر : دسویں حصہ کا آدھا یعنی بیسواں حصہ، جس کو میں نے دو چالیسواں حصہ کہا، دو چالیسواں حصہ ملا کر بیسواں حصہ بن جاتا ہے۔ ثلاثة ارباع : تین چالیسواں حصہ۔
[ ۴۶۵ ] (۳) حضرت امام ابو یوسف اور محمد نے فرما یا زیادتی میں کوئی چیز نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ ساٹھ تک پہنچ جائے ، پس ساٹھ میں دو بچھڑے یا دو بچھڑیاں ہیں۔ ساتھ دو مرتبہ میں تمہیں ہو جاتے ہیں اور ایک تمہیں میں بچھڑا ہے اس لئے دومرتبہ میں میں دو بچھڑے لازم ہونگے۔
عن ابن عباس قال لما بعث رسول الله معاذا الى اليمن قيل له بما امرت قال امرت ان اخذ من البقر من كل ثلاثين تبيـعـا او تبيعة ومن كل اربعين مسنة قيل له امرت في الاوقاص بشيء ؟ قال لا وسأسال النبي الله فساله فقال لا وهو مابين السنيـن يـعـنـى لا تأخذ من ذلك شيئا (الف) (دار قطنی ۳ باب لیس فی الکسرشی و ج ثانی ص ۸۰ نمبر ۱۸۸۷ار مصنف ابن ابی هیة ، ۱۵ فى الزيادة في الفريضة ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۳۶۴، نمبر (۹۹۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وقص میں کوئی زکوۃ نہیں ہے اور چالیس سے لیکر ساٹھ تک وقص ہے اس لئے اس میں بھی کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
وقص : دو عمروں کے درمیان یا دو عددوں کے درمیان جو عدد ہو اس کو اوقاص کہتے ہیں۔
(2) When (the number) increases beyond forty, then upon the increase, according to that (ratio) up to sixty, according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), is obligatory: in one (cow), one-fortieth of a musinnah; in two, two-fortieths of a musinnah; in three, three-fourths of a tenth of a musinnah. (3) And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is nothing in the increase until it reaches sixty, then in it (sixty) are two tabi' or two tabi'ah. Explanation: 'rub'u 'ushr' means one-fourth of a tenth, i.e., one-fortieth; 'nisfu 'ushr' means half of a tenth, i.e., one-twentieth, which I called two-fortieths; joining two-fortieths makes one-twentieth. 'Thalathatu arba' 'ushr' means three-fortieths. (3) Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: There is nothing in the increase until it reaches sixty, then in sixty are two calves or two heifers. Because sixty consists of two (sets of) thirty, and in each thirty is a calf, so in two sets, two calves are obligatory. From Ibn Abbas: When the Messenger of Allah sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he was asked 'With what were you commanded?' He said: 'I was commanded to take from cows: from every thirty, a tabi' or a tabi'ah, and from every forty, a musinnah.' He was asked: 'Were you commanded anything regarding the waqs (intervening numbers)?' He said: 'No.' Then he asked the Prophet, and he said: 'No, and it is what is between the two ages,' meaning do not take anything from that. (Dar Qutni, Ibn Abi Shayba) From this hadith it is known that there is no zakat on the waqs, and the numbers between forty and sixty are waqs, so nothing is obligatory in them. Waqs: the number between two numbers is called awqas.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the zakat on cows between 40 and 60. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that any increase above 40 up to 60 incurs a proportional zakat: for one extra cow, one-fortieth of a musinnah; for two, two-fortieths; for three, three-fortieths, etc. This is based on the principle that zakat increases proportionally (as supported by an athar from Makhul). In contrast, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that no zakat is due on the excess until the total reaches 60, at which point two tabi' (yearlings) are due. Their evidence is the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet explicitly said there is no zakat on al-awqas (the interval numbers). The term 'waqs' is defined as the number between two fixed nisab thresholds. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Abu Hanifa's view, one must pay fractional amounts for extra cows, whereas under the Sahibayn, no payment is made until 60. The text does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but later Hanafi practice often relies on the Sahibayn's position for caution.

Key Terms
وقص (waqs): The number between two fixed nisab thresholds (e.g., between 40 and 60).
زیادہ (ziyadah): Increase above the nisab number.
musinnah (musinnah): A cow that has entered its third year (two years old).
tabi' (tabi'): A calf that has completed one year and entered the second.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited by the Sahibayn, what did the Prophet say about zakat on al-awqas?
A) 'Take a musinnah for every forty'
B) 'Do not take anything from that'
C) 'Take a tabi' for every thirty'
D) 'Calculate proportionally'

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for cows between 40 and 60 centers on whether the explicit hadith on awqas overrides the qiyas of proportionality.

Zakat on 70, 80, and 90 Cows
Lists zakat due for 70, 80, 90 cows combining nisab units

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate zakat due on 70, 80, and 90 cows by combining nisab thresholds of 30 and 40 cows.

Core Idea
Combine nisab units: 70 = 30+40 gives one tabi' and one musinnah.

The zakat on cattle depends on the number owned. For cows, the nisab starts at 30, where one tabi' (one-year-old) is due; at 40, one musinnah (two-year-old) is due. For numbers in between, the obligation is computed by grouping into these units. This lesson applies the rule to 70, 80, and 90 cows, showing how the standard Hanafi position derives from the basic nisabs.

Guided Path
1
Recall the nisab thresholds
For 30–39 cows: one tabi'. For 40–59 cows: one musinnah. For 60–69: two tabi'. These patterns repeat.
2
Break the number into groups of 30 and 40
70 = 30 + 40; 80 = 40 + 40; 90 = 30 + 30 + 30. Split the total into these fundamental units.
90 is three groups of 30 because 60 is two groups of 30, and 90 adds another 30.
3
Assign zakat per group
Each group of 30 yields one tabi'. Each group of 40 yields one musinnah.
A group of 30 always gives a tabi'; a group of 40 always gives a musinnah.
4
Combine the obligations
Add together the tabi' and musinnah from each group. For 70: one tabi' (from 30) + one musinnah (from 40). For 80: two musinnah (from two 40s). For 90: three tabi' (from three 30s).
No mixing of types beyond what the groups produce.

Source Text

[۴۶۷] (۵) وفي ثمانين مسنتان
[۴۶۸] (٦) وفي تسعين ثلثة اتبعة.
اور ستر میں ایک مسنہ اور ایک تبیعہ ہوں گے۔
اس لئے کہ ایک تھیں اور ایک چالیس کا مجموعہ ستر ہے۔
اور اسی (۸۰) میں دومسنہ ہوں گے۔
اس میں دو مرتبہ چالیس چالیس ہوتے ہیں اور چالیس میں ایک مسنہ ہے اس لئے اسی میں دومسنہ ہوں گے۔
اور نوے میں تین بچھڑے ہوں گے۔
(4) And in seventy: one musinnah and one tabi'. (5) And in eighty: two musinnah. (6) And in ninety: three tabi'. And in seventy there will be one musinnah and one tabi'. Because seventy is (the sum of) thirty and forty. And in eighty (80) there will be two musinnah. Because in it there are two forties, and in forty is one musinnah, so in eighty there will be two musinnah. And in ninety there will be three calves.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage lists the zakat obligations for 70, 80, and 90 cows, which are derived by combining the basic nisab units: 70 = 30 + 40, so it combines the zakat of both: one tabi' (from 30) and one musinnah (from 40). 80 = 40 + 40, so two musinnah. 90 = 30 + 30 + 30, so three tabi'. No dispute is mentioned; these are standard rulings after the earlier ikhtilaf. The author simply states these as the established positions.

Key Terms
مسنة (musinnah): A cow that has completed two years (a two-year-old).
تبيع (tabi'): A calf that has completed one year (a one-year-old).
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Zakat on cows is calculated by breaking the total into groups of 30 and 40 and summing the individual obligations.

The Ruling on Intermediate Numbers (Awqas) in Cow Zakah
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and schedule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on zakah for awqas, identify the relied-upon position, and apply the zakah schedule for cows from 30 to 100.

Core Idea
No zakah on cows between 40 and 60 because the explicit hadith overrides qiyas.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa, using qiyas, argues that zakah is due proportionally on each cow above 40 until 60. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, citing a clear hadith, hold that no zakah is due on these intermediate numbers. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn. The passage then provides the full zakah schedule for cows from 30 to 100, and extends the ruling to buffaloes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
Focus on the cows between 41 and 59. This range is called 'awqas' (intermediate numbers). The question is whether zakah applies to each animal individually.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Imam Abu Hanifa: for each cow above 40, a fraction of a musinnah (1/40 per cow) until 60. Abu Yusuf & Muhammad: nothing is due until 60; then two tabi's.
Both positions are within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the dalil
The hadith of Mu'adh (radiAllahu anhu) explicitly exempts the awqas. This is a clear text (nass) that overrides qiyas in Hanafi usul.
The text quotes the hadith: 'La' (no) regarding the awqas.
4
Apply the mufta bihi position
For any number between 40 and 60 (e.g., 45, 58), no zakah is due. Only at 60 does a new nisab trigger two tabi's.
5
Extend to the full schedule
The passage gives fixed amounts for 70, 80, 90, 100 cows, showing alternation every ten between tabi' and musinnah. Buffaloes are identical.
Review the table in the source to internalize the pattern.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الأوّل
كتاب الزكوة
[۴۹](۷) وفى مائة تبيعتان و مسنة [۴۷۰] (۸) وعلى هذا يتغير الفرض في كل عشرة
من تبيع الى مسنة [۴۷۱](۹) والجواميس والبقر سواء.

ایک تبیعہ
ایک مسند
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Volume 1, Book of Zakah. When [the number of cows] reaches forty, [zakah] is due on the increase proportionally up to sixty according to Abu Hanifa: so on one [increase] is 1/40 of a musinnah, on two is 1/20 of a musinnah, on three is 3/40 of a musinnah [465](3). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: there is nothing in the increase until it reaches sixty, then there are two tabi' or two tabi'at [466](4). And at seventy: one musinnah and one tabi' [467](5). And at eighty: two musinnahs [468](6). And at ninety: three atiba' (plural of tabi'). Explanation: rabu' ushr = a quarter of a tenth, i.e., 1/40; nisf ushr = half of a tenth, i.e., 1/20; three fourths = 3/40. [465](3): Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: there is nothing in the increase until it reaches sixty, then at sixty there are two male or female calves. Since 60 equals two 30s, and each 30 requires a calf, so two calves are necessary. From Ibn Abbas: When the Messenger of Allah sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he was asked: With what were you commanded? He said: I was commanded to take from every 30 cattle a tabi' or tabi'ah, and from every 40 a musinnah. He was asked: Were you commanded to take anything from the awqas? He said: No, but I will ask the Prophet. So he asked, and he said: No, meaning the animals between the ages [i.e., do not take anything from that] (al-Daraqutni, etc.) This hadith shows that there is no zakah on the waqs, and the period from 40 to 60 is al-waqs, so nothing is required in it either. Waqs: the number between two ages or two numbers is called awqas. [466](4): And at seventy there will be one musinnah and one tabi'ah, because 70 = 30 + 40, so [the zakah] is one from each. [467](5): And at eighty there will be two musinnahs, because 80 = two 40s. [468](6): And at ninety there will be three calves, because 90 = three 30s. Marginal note (a): The hadith with details. [49](7): And at one hundred there are two tabi'at and one musinnah [470](8): And on this basis the obligation changes every ten from tabi' to musinnah [471](9): And buffaloes and cows are the same. At ninety there are three sets of 30, so three calves. [469](7): And at one hundred cows there are two calves and one musinnah, because 100 = 60 + 40. [470](8): Similarly the calculation changes every ten from tabi' to musinnah. The difference between 30 and 40 is ten numbers, so when the number increases by ten, if a musinnah was required, a tabi' becomes required, and if a tabi' was required, a musinnah becomes required. So every ten it alternates between tabi' and musinnah. Tabi' means a calf. [471](9): In this matter, buffaloes and cows are equal. The calculation mentioned for cows applies also to buffaloes, because they are of close species. Table: [A table showing zakah amounts for cows from 30 to 130 appears, but is corrupted in OCR].
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the ruling on zakah for cows when the number falls between the fixed nisabs (40 and 60). The underlying issue is whether the 'awqas' (intermediate numbers between 41 and 59) require zakah. Imam Abu Hanifa, relying on qiyas (analogy) with the progressive nature of zakah on other wealth, argues that each additional animal above 40 incurs a proportional fraction of a musinnah (1/40, 2/40, etc. up to 60). In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad adhere to the literal reading of the hadith of Mu'adh (radiAllahu anhu), where the Prophet (sallAllahu alayhi wa sallam) explicitly stated that nothing is due on the awqas (the animals between the prescribed ages). The Sahibayn therefore assert that no zakah is due on any number between 41 and 59; only when the herd reaches 60 does a new nisab apply, requiring two tabi's. The text then proceeds to list the fixed zakah obligations for 70, 80, 90, and 100 cows, showing the pattern: at 70 (40+30) one musinnah and one tabi'; at 80 (two 40s) two musinnahs; at 90 (three 30s) three tabi's; at 100 (60+40) two tabi's and one musinnah. The author explains that every increase of ten causes the required animal to alternate between tabi' (for multiples of 30) and musinnah (for multiples of 40). Finally, the ruling is extended to buffaloes, as they are considered the same genus (jins) as cows for zakah purposes. The authoritative weight of this passage is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as the base ruling (the matn) is from al-Quduri, and the commentary (sharh) expands upon it. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), i.e., no zakah on the awqas, because the hadith is clear and the qiyas of Abu Hanifa is overridden by this explicit textual evidence.

Key Terms
تَبِیع (tabīʿ): A male calf that has completed one year and entered the second year, i.e., one year old.
مُسِنَّة (musinnah): A female cow that has entered its third year, i.e., two years old.
أَوْقَاص (awqas): The numbers between the fixed nisabs (for cows, between 40 and 60).
جواميس (jawāmīs): Buffaloes; treated identically to cows for zakah purposes according to this text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how much zakah is due on 59 cows?
A) 1/40 of a musinnah
B) 1 tabi'
C) Nothing
D) 2 tabi's

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the explicit hadith exempting the awqas (40-60) overrides qiyas, so no zakah is due on cows between 41 and 59.

Zakat Rates for Cows: The Alternating Rule of Tabi' and Musinnah
Ruling statement with expansion on zakat rates for cows and buffaloes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi zakat rates for cows from 30 to 120 head and apply the rule that the required animal alternates every ten head between tabi' and musinnah.

Core Idea
For cows and buffaloes, zakat animals swap between tabi' and musinnah every ten head beyond the nisab.

Zakat on cattle follows a precise schedule set by the Prophet (peace be upon him). The Hanafi school details this schedule for cows and buffaloes, with an alternating pattern: as the herd increases by ten, the type of animal due changes. This lesson unpacks that pattern and clarifies that buffaloes are treated identically to cows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab and initial rates
For cows, zakat becomes wajib at 30 head. From 30-39, one tabi' (calf aged 1-2 years) is due. From 40-49, one musinnah (cow aged 2-3 years) is due.
Tabi' and musinnah are the two categories of animals required.
2
Understand the alternating pattern
Every increase of ten cows changes the required animal. For example, 50-59 requires one tabi' and one musinnah; 60-69 requires two tabi'; 70-79 requires one musinnah and two tabi'? The text states 'upon this the obligation changes every ten from tabi' to musinnah'.
The pattern is derived by grouping intervals of 30 and 40.
3
Apply to specific numbers
Given a number of cows, determine the zakat due by grouping into intervals of 30 and 40. For example, 100 cows = 60 (2 tabi') + 40 (1 musinnah) = total 2 tabi' + 1 musinnah.
The Urdu commentary explains that 100 cows consist of 60 and 40.
4
Extend to buffaloes
Buffaloes (jawaamis) are ruled exactly like cows for zakat purposes. All the same rates and alternating pattern apply.
This is a key Hanafi position; other schools may differ.

Source Text

And on one hundred, two tabi' and one musinnah. (8) And upon this the obligation changes every ten from tabi' to musinnah. (9) And buffaloes and cows are equal.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi ruling on zakat for cows (baqar) and buffaloes (jawaamis). It gives the specific obligation: for 100 cows, two tabi' (one-year-old calves) and one musinnah (two-year-old cow) are due. The rule is that for every ten cows beyond the nisab, the required animal switches between tabi' and musinnah. For example, from 30-39: one tabi'; 40-49: one musinnah; 50-59: one tabi' and one musinnah; 60-69: two tabi'; and so on. The text emphasizes that buffaloes are treated identically to cows in zakat calculations. The Urdu commentary explains the reasoning: 100 cows consist of two groups of 30 and one group of 40, hence two tabi' and one musinnah. The cycle continues with every ten increase.

Key Terms
تبيع (tabi'): A male or female calf that has completed one year and entered the second year.
مسنة (musinnah): A cow that has completed two years and entered the third year.
جواميس (jawaamis): Buffaloes (plural of jamus).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Two tabi'
D) One tabi' and one musinnah

Key Takeaway
For cows and buffaloes, the Hanafi zakat obligation alternates between tabi' and musinnah every additional ten head beyond the nisab.

Zakat on Goats: Nisab Thresholds and the Proof
Explains nisab thresholds for zakat on goats with textual proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab thresholds for zakat on goats and explain the hadith proof that establishes the ruling.

Core Idea
Zakat on goats is due at specific thresholds, not per goat; the proof is the hadith of Abu Bakr's letter.

Zakat on livestock is a wajib obligation when conditions are met. This passage focuses on goats (and sheep) and details the precise nisab brackets. The matn provides a clear schedule, and the commentary resolves an apparent discrepancy with the supporting hadith. By the end, you will confidently know how much zakat is due for any herd size.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its conditions
The act is giving zakat on goats. The conditions are: the goats must be sā'ima (grazing), and a full lunar year (hawl) must pass. Nisab begins at 40 goats.
Without sā'ima or hawl, zakat is not wajib.
2
Memorize the nisab brackets
From the matn: 40-120 goats → 1 goat; 121-200 → 2 goats; 201-399 → 3 goats; 400 exactly → 4 goats; then for every hundred above, 1 goat.
Note: the per-hundred rule starts at 400 in the matn but is adjusted by the hadith (see next step).
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith from Abu Bakr's letter states the same brackets but says: after 300, in every hundred one goat. This is the relied-upon proof (Bukhari, Abu Dawud).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted in fiqh al-zakat.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction
The matn says per-hundred starts at 400, the hadith at 300. The commentary explains: the matn mentions 400 as the point where the per-hundred rule takes effect after listing fixed brackets; effectively, after 300 the per-hundred rule applies. There is no contradiction.
The mufta bihi is the hadith's version: after 300, one per hundred.
5
Apply the ruling to a herd size
Take a herd of 350 goats: 201-399 gives 3 goats. For 400: 4 goats. For 500: first 400 give 4, plus 1 for the next 100 = 5 goats. Use the rule consistently.
Always count from the lowest bracket upward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صدقة الغنم
ليس في اقل من اربعين شاة صدقة فاذا كانت اربعين شاة سائمة وحال عليها الحول ففيها شاة الى مائة وعشرين فاذا زادت واحدة ففيها شاتان الى مائتين فاذا زادت واحدة ففيها ثلث شياة فاذا بلغت اربع مائة ففيها اربع شاة ثم في كل مائة شاة.

تشريح: چالیس سے ایک سو بیس کے درمیان بکریوں میں ایک بکری زکوۃ کی ہے پھر ایک سو اکیس سے دوسو تک میں دو بکریاں ہیں۔اور دوسو ایک سے تین سو نناوے تک تین بکریاں ہیں۔ اور چار سو بکریوں میں چار بکریاں زکوۃ ہیں۔ پھر ہر اک سو میں ایک بکری زکوۃ لازم ہوگی۔

حدیث میں ہے: ان انسا حدثه ان ابا بكر كتب له هذا الكتاب لما وجهه الى البحرين بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم هذه فريضة الصدقة التى فرض رسول الله على المسلمين والتي امر الله به رسوله ... وفي صدقة الغنم في سائمتها اذا كانت اربعين الى عشرين ومائة شاةً، فاذا زادت على عشرين ومائة الى مائتين شاتان، فاذا زادت على مائتين الى ثلث ماة ففيها ثلاث، فاذا زادت على ثلث مائة ففي كل مائة شأة ، فاذا كانت سائمة الرجل ناقصة من اربعين شاة واحدة فليس فيها صدقة الا ان يشاء ربها.

اس حدیث سے اوپر کے حساب کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ البتہ حدیث میں ہے کہ دوسو ایک سے تین سوتک تین بکریاں ہوں گی اور تین سو کے بعد ہر سو میں ایک بکری لازم ہوگی ۔ اور متن میں تھا کہ چارسو کے بعد ہرسو میں ایک بکری لازم ہوگی ۔ اس میں تعارض نہیں کیونکہ متن میں چارسو کا ذکر اس لئے ہے کہ اس سے پہلے کی تفصیل بیان کی گئی ہے۔
Chapter of Zakat of Goats: There is no zakat on less than forty goats. When there are forty grazing goats and a year passes, then in them is one goat up to one hundred twenty. When it increases by one (i.e., becomes one hundred twenty-one), then in them are two goats up to two hundred. When it increases by one (i.e., becomes two hundred one), then in them are three goats up to three hundred ninety-nine. When it reaches four hundred, then in them are four goats. Then in every hundred is one goat. Commentary: Between forty and one hundred twenty goats, one goat is zakat. Then from one hundred twenty-one to two hundred, two goats. And from two hundred one to three hundred ninety-nine, three goats. And at four hundred goats, four goats. Then every hundred requires one goat. Hadith: Anas narrated that Abu Bakr wrote this book when he sent him to Bahrain: In the zakat of grazing goats, when they are forty to one hundred twenty, one goat; when they increase beyond one hundred twenty to two hundred, two goats; when they increase beyond two hundred to three hundred, three goats; when they increase beyond three hundred, in every hundred one goat. If a man's grazing goats are less than forty, no zakat is due unless the owner wishes. This hadith supports the above calculation. However, the hadith says from two hundred one to three hundred, three goats, and after three hundred, one goat per hundred. The matn said after four hundred, one goat per hundred. There is no contradiction because the matn mentioned four hundred as the point from which the per-hundred rule starts, having already covered the preceding thresholds.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the nisab thresholds for zakat on goats, supported by a hadith from the practice of Abu Bakr (رضي الله عنه). The matn (from Quduri or similar) states: No zakat on less than 40 goats. For 40-120 goats, zakat is 1 goat. For 121-200, 2 goats. For 201-399, 3 goats. For 400 exactly, 4 goats. Then for every hundred above, 1 goat. The Urdu commentary clarifies these thresholds and notes an apparent discrepancy: the hadith says after 300, every hundred gives one goat, while the matn says after 400. The commentator resolves this by explaining that the matn's mention of 400 is the point where the per-hundred rule takes effect after listing the previous fixed amounts; effectively, after 300, the per-hundred rule applies (as per hadith). The hadith confirms the same thresholds except it starts the per-hundred rule from 300 onward. The Hanafi position is that the nisab for goats is as stated, and the ruling is based on this hadith which is considered sound. The hadith is from Abu Bakr's letter, cited in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.

Key Terms
سائمة (sā'ima): Grazing livestock that are pastured for most of the year, not stall-fed.
شاة (shāt): A single goat or sheep, used generically for small livestock.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 2 goats
B) 3 goats
C) 4 goats
D) 5 goats

Key Takeaway
Zakat on goats is due at fixed brackets (40, 121, 201, 400) and then per hundred after 300 (per hadith), with the condition of sā'ima and hawl.

Sheep and Goats: One Category for Zakat Calculation
Ruling statement with nisab table

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sheep and goats are equivalent for zakat and apply the unified nisab table to calculate zakat on mixed flocks.

Core Idea
Sheep and goats are one type for zakat — combine them to reach nisab.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling from the Hanafi school: the equivalence of sheep (الضان) and goats (المعز) for zakat. The source text states this principle clearly, then provides the nisab schedule. Understanding this rule is essential for accurate zakat calculation when a person owns both sheep and goats.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text says 'Sheep and goats are equal.' This means they are treated as one category for zakat nisab and calculation.
This is a distinct Hanafi position.
2
Memorize the nisab threshold
The nisab is 40 head. At 40, zakat is one goat/sheep.
This is the minimum threshold.
3
Memorize the schedule increments
For 121 head, two animals; 201 head, three; 400 head, four; 500 head, five. Note the pattern: after the first 40, the next bracket is 121 (increase of 81), then 201 (increase of 80), then 400 (increase of 199), then 500 (increase of 100).
The schedule is the same as for sheep alone.
4
Apply to mixed flock
Combine the count of sheep and goats to determine if nisab is reached and calculate zakat using the unified schedule.
For example, 30 sheep + 15 goats = 45 → nisab met, zakat: 1 animal.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn establishing that sheep (الضان) and goats (المعز) are treated as a single category for zakat. The Urdu commentary explains that despite minor differences, the ruling is uniform. The table provides the zakat schedule for goats, analogous to sheep: at 40 goats, one goat is due; at 121, two; at 201, three; at 400, four; at 500, five; and so on, following the same nisab and rates as sheep. This principle simplifies calculation because the two animals are considered one genus (جنس) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الضان (al-dān): Sheep, specifically domesticated ovines.
المعز (al-ma‘z): Goats, domesticated caprines.
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation. For sheep/goats: 40 head.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, sheep and goats are one type for zakat; combine to reach nisab, and the zakat schedule is the same as for sheep alone.

Zakat on Horses: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute over zakat on pasturing horses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for zakat on horses according to Abu Hanifa, explain why the Sahibayn disagree, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Breeding pasturing horses attract zakat; war and work horses do not.

This passage from Bab Zakat al-Khayl presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether pasturing horses are subject to zakat. Abu Hanifa obligates zakat on horses that are both male and female and have been pasturing, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no zakat is due on pasturing horses at all. The disagreement hinges on how to reconcile conflicting hadith evidence and the purpose of the horses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for zakat on horses according to the matn
Note that the horses must be sa'imah (pasturing), include both genders, and a full year must pass. The owner has an option to pay per head or value-based.
2
State the dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa obligates zakat on pasturing horses with both genders; the Sahibayn say no zakat on pasturing horses at all.
3
Examine the evidence for each position
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith from Jabir commanding one dinar per horse; the Sahibayn rely on hadiths stating no sadaqah on horses and istihsan.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn's objection
Hanafi scholars interpret the conflicting hadiths as referring to work or war horses, not breeding horses.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, so zakat is due on breeding horses; but some later fatwas adopt the Sahibayn for ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكوة الخيل (۱) اذا كانت الخيل سائمة ذكورا و اناثا و حال عليها الحول فصاحبها بالخيار ان شاء اعطى عن كل فرس دينار او ان شاء قومها فاعطى عن كل مائتي درهم خمسة دراهم (۲) وليس في ذكورها منفردة زكوة عند ابي حنيفة (۳) وقال ابو يوسف ومحمد لا زكاة في الخيل السائمة. الدليل: عن جابر قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الخيل السائمة في كل فرس دينار تؤديه. (رواه الدارقطني والبيهقي). ضروری نوٹ گھوڑے کے سلسلہ میں کئی قسم کی احادیث ہیں۔ اس لئے علماء میں اختلاف ہے کہ گھوڑے میں زکوۃ واجب ہے یا نہیں۔ یہ بات طے ہے کہ جہاد کے گھوڑے میں اور خدمت کے گھوڑے میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ اور تجارت کے گھوڑے میں اس کی قیمت میں ہر دو سو درہم میں پانچ درہم لازم ہے۔ البتہ جو گھوڑے نسل بڑھانے کے لئے ہیں ان ہی میں اختلاف ہے کہ زکوۃ واجب ہے یا نہیں ؟ اور ہر ایک امام کا مسئلہ اور اس کی دلیل آگے آرہی ہے۔
Chapter of Zakat on Horses. (1) If horses are pasturing (sa'imah), males and females, and a year passes, then their owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives for every horse one dinar; or if he wishes, he values them and gives for every two hundred dirhams five dirhams. (2) And there is no zakat on male horses alone according to Abu Hanifa. (3) And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: No zakat on pasturing horses. The evidence: from Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Concerning pasturing horses, for every horse you will pay one dinar.' (Narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi). Essential note: Regarding horses, there are various hadiths. Therefore there is disagreement among scholars whether zakat is obligatory on horses or not. It is settled that there is no zakat on war horses and work horses. And on trade horses, on their value, for every two hundred dirhams five dirhams is due. However, regarding horses kept for breeding, there is disagreement whether zakat is obligatory or not. The ruling of each Imam and its evidence are given below.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on zakat of horses (Bab Zakat al-Khayl) presents the ruling and the intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states the basic ruling: for pasturing horses (sa'imah) that are both male and female and have reached a full year, the owner has an option to give either one dinar per horse or 2.5% of their market value (five dirhams per two hundred dirhams). Then it notes that according to Abu Hanifa, if the horses are only males (no females), no zakat is due because they cannot breed. Then the passage cites the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that there is no zakat at all on pasturing horses, whether males or females. The evidence for the ruling is the hadith from Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded one dinar per horse for pasturing horses. The Urdu commentary adds that war horses and work horses are exempt, and trade horses follow the general trade zakat rule. The dispute is specifically about breeding horses. Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith and analogizes breeding horses to livestock (an'am) because they produce offspring. The Sahibayn restrict the hadith or consider it abrogated, as other evidence suggests no zakat on horses. The relied-upon position in the school is the view of Abu Hanifa, as the hadith is authentic and the ruling of zakat on horses is established by it. However, later fatwa practice often follows the Sahibayn view due to the difficulty of applying the dinar-per-head rate.

Key Terms
خيل سائمة (khayl sā'imah): Horses that graze freely on pasture for the majority of the year without being fed by the owner.
ذكورا و اناثا (dhukūran wa ināthan): Both male and female horses together; the presence of both genders is a condition for zakat according to Abu Hanifa.
توالد وتناسل (tawālud wa tanāsul): Breeding and procreation; the reason why male-only horses are not zakatable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when is zakat wajib on horses?
A) Only on male horses
B) On both male and female horses that are pasturing and a year passes
C) On all horses regardless of purpose
D) Only on female horses

Key Takeaway
Pasturing breeding horses with both genders are subject to zakat in the Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, despite the Sahibayn's dissent.

Zakat on Horses, Mules, and Donkeys
Ruling on zakat for horses, mules, and donkeys with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat for horses, mules, and donkeys and identify the condition that triggers zakat obligation.

Core Idea
Horses, mules, and donkeys are zakat-free unless they are trade goods.

This lesson addresses a common question: do animals we ride or work with incur zakat? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on authentic hadith. You will learn the default exemption and the exception for trade animals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The passage rules on whether zakat is due on horses, mules, and donkeys. The base ruling is no zakat (mubah).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his horse and his slave.' This hadith is cited from Abu Hurairah and recorded by Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation of sadaqah (zakat) on horses indicates no obligation. Hanafis interpret this as general, covering all horses unless they become trade goods.
Imam Abu Hanifa clarifies the exemption is for jihad and daily work horses.
4
Note the condition
The exception: if these animals are intended for trade, they become trade goods and zakat is due on their value (2.5% per nisab).
This is based on istihsan – analogizing to merchandise.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling is consistent with the apparent meaning of the hadith. Other schools may impose zakat on pastured horses, but Hanafis prioritize the explicit text.
The mufta bihi is no zakat on non-trade animals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, part one, 310. Book of Zakat. Yusuf and Muhammad: No zakat on horses. [477] (4) And nothing on mules and donkeys except if they are for trade. [478] (5) And there is no zakat on young camels, young sheep, and young cows according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad unless there are adults with them. Dirhams become obligatory because now it is trade goods, and on trade goods there is zakat. Their proof is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah said: The Prophet said: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim for his horse and his slave.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that there is no zakat on a Muslim's horses. Imam Abu Hanifa says: This refers to horses used for jihad and daily work. [477] (4) There is no zakat on mules and donkeys unless they are for trade. If mules and donkeys are for trade, then they become trade goods, so according to trade goods, on their value every two hundred dirhams five dirhams zakat. But if they are not for trade but for breeding, there is no zakat on them. The proof is this hadith: From Abu Hurairah said: 'I said: O Messenger of Allah, what about donkeys?' He said: 'Nothing has been revealed to me about donkeys except this comprehensive verse: Whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it.' (Muslim, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) From this hadith it is understood that there is no zakat on donkeys, and mules are a type of donkey, so there is no zakat on them either.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof on zakat for horses, mules, and donkeys. The matn states that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two disciples of Abu Hanifa), there is no zakat on horses. The commentator expands by citing the hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet exempted horses and slaves from zakat. This hadith provides the proof for the ruling. Imam Abu Hanifa clarifies that this exemption applies to horses used for jihad and daily work, implying that horses kept solely for trade would incur zakat. For mules and donkeys, the base ruling is no zakat unless they are trade goods. The commentator again provides a hadith from Abu Hurairah where the Prophet states that nothing was revealed about donkeys except the general verse of good and evil. This indicates no specific obligation. The Hanafi position is clear: working animals are exempt; trade animals are subject to zakat on their value. Note: In the Hanafi madhhab, there is no zakat on horses, mules, or donkeys that are not intended for trade (authority_weight: Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
زكوة (zakāt): The obligatory alms given on specific categories of wealth in the Hanafi madhhab.
خيل (khyal): Horses; in this context, animals that are exempt from zakat unless they are trade goods.
بغال (bighāl): Mules; hybrids of a horse and donkey. Ruled like donkeys in zakat.
حمير (himār): Donkeys; exempt from zakat unless for trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, regardless of use
B) Only if they are used for riding
C) Only if they are intended for trade
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The default ruling is no zakat on horses, mules, and donkeys; zakat becomes due only if they are intended for trade.

Zakat on Young Livestock: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for young camels, sheep, and cows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on zakat for young livestock, explain the evidence each side uses, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Young livestock are not zakatable unless accompanied by adults.

This lesson examines a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute: whether zakat is due on young camels, sheep, and cows when no adult animals are present. The disagreement turns on two conflicting reports from the tabi'un and differing views on whether young animals contribute to the nisab. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the school's tarjih methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
List the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (no zakat on young alone) and the ruling of Abu Yusuf (zakat due on young alone if nisab is met).
Both are Hanafi imams; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Examine the evidence for each side
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad cite the athar from al-Hasan: 'The young sheep is not counted nor taken in sadaqah.' Abu Yusuf cites the athar from Ata: 'Young sheep are counted.'
Both athar are from the Musannaf of Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Understand the reasoning behind each position
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that young animals do not increase in number (nasl) independently; they only grow older. Thus, without adults, the nisab is not considered complete. Abu Yusuf holds that the nisab itself is based on count, and young animals count like adults.
This is also a difference in how 'nisab' is interpreted.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position and its rationale
The relied-upon fatwa follows Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The athar from al-Hasan is preferred, and the principle of avoiding a weak position (tarjih) supports this choice.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah adopted this view.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a person who owns 40 young sheep (no adults). According to the mufta bihi, no zakat is due. According to Abu Yusuf, one young sheep is due. Test your understanding.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ومن وجب عليه مسن فلم يوجد اخذ المصدق اعلى منها ورد الفضل او اخذ دونها واخذ الفضل. ا : الفصلان : فصیل کی جمع ہے اونٹنی کے بچے ۔ الحملان : حمل کی جمع ہے بکری کے بچے۔ العجا جیل : مجمول کی جمع ہے گائے کے نہیں ہوتی تو چھوٹے بچے تمیں سے کم ہوں تو کیسے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ اسی طرح چالیس بکری کے بچے ہوں تو ان میں ایک بچہ لازم ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ بڑی بکری کا نصاب یہی ہے ۔ اور اگر بکری کے چالیس بچوں سے کم ہوں تو زکوۃ لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح پچھیں اونٹنی کے بچے ہوں تو ان میں ایک بچہ لازم ہو گا اس سے کم ہو تو لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن عطاء قال قلت له يعتد بالصغار اولاد الشاة؟ قال نعم (الف ) مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۴ السخلة تحسب على صاحب الغنم - ج ثانی ص ۱۳۶۸ نمبر ۹۹۸۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بکری کے بچوں کا بھی شمار ہوگا اور اس کی زکوۃ لازم ہوگی۔
And there is no zakat on young camels, young sheep, and young cows according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad unless there are adults with them. [478] (5) In the young camels, young sheep, and young cows, according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, there is no zakat unless adults are with them. If adults are with these young, then the young are subordinated to the adults and zakat becomes obligatory. But if there are no adults, then there is no possibility of increase in number; rather the young will grow up but there will be no increase in count, so there is no zakat on them. Their proof is this narration: From al-Hasan: 'The young sheep (sakhla) is not counted nor taken in sadaqah.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) From this it is understood that young sheep are not counted for zakat. By analogy, young camels and young cows also have no zakat unless there are adults with them. Footnotes: ... [479] (6) And Abu Yusuf said: Zakat is obligatory on them, one animal from them. [480] And from one upon whom a musinn (specific age) is obligatory and he does not have it, the collector takes a higher grade and returns the excess, or takes a lower grade and takes the excess. (Definitions of terms) ... [479] (6) Imam Abu Yusuf said: One young animal becomes obligatory on them. That is, if you have young cows, then one young cow is obligatory, not less. Because if the number is less than the nisab of adult cows, zakat is not obligatory, so if young are less, how can zakat be obligatory? Similarly, if there are forty young sheep, one young sheep becomes obligatory, because that is the nisab of adult sheep. If less than forty, no zakat. Similarly, if there are five young camels, one young camel becomes obligatory; less than that, not obligatory. His proof is this narration: From Ata: 'I said to him: Are young offspring of sheep counted? He said: Yes.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) From this it is understood that young sheep are counted and their zakat is obligatory.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat on young livestock (camels, sheep, cows). The matn first states the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: no zakat on young animals unless they are accompanied by adults. The commentator explains the reasoning: young animals lack potential for increase in number (nasl) until they mature; with adults, the young follow the adult nisab. Their proof is an athar from al-Hasan that young sheep are not counted for zakat. Then the text presents Abu Yusuf's opposing view: zakat is due on young animals if they reach the nisab (e.g., 40 young sheep, 5 young camels). He cites an athar from Ata that young sheep are counted. The disagreement hinges on whether young livestock are considered independently for zakat. The Hanafi school's ruling (mufta bihi) is that young animals are not zakatable on their own unless they are part of a herd with adults (authority_weight: Zahir al-Riwayah). This ikhtilaf has practical implications: if someone owns only young livestock, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, no zakat; according to Abu Yusuf, zakat is due once they reach the nisab. The commentator uses qiyas (analogy) to extend the ruling on sheep to camels and cows.

Key Terms
فصلان (fiṣlān): Plural of fiṣl, young camel (less than one year old).
حملان (ḥimlān): Plural of ḥamal, young sheep (usually from birth to one year).
عجاجيل (ʿajājīl): Plural of ʿijl, young cow (calf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab (mufta bihi), if someone owns 50 young sheep with no adult sheep, is zakat due?
A) Yes, zakat on one young sheep
B) No zakat because there are no adults
C) Yes, zakat on the value
D) No zakat because sheep are exempt

Key Takeaway
Zakat on young livestock is not due unless adult animals are present; this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Substituting Zakat Animals When Exact Age Is Unavailable
Ruling on substituting zakat animal when exact age unavailable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substituting a higher or lower grade zakat animal when the required age is unavailable, and apply the compensation rules from the hadith of Abu Bakr.

Core Idea
When the exact zakat animal is missing, the collector may take a higher grade with a refund or a lower grade with payment.

Zakat on livestock requires giving an animal of a specific age. But what if the owner does not have that exact age? This lesson explains the Hanafi concession based on the practice of Caliph Abu Bakr: substitution is allowed with monetary adjustment. This ensures the zakat obligation can be fulfilled without imposing undue hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states that the collector may take a higher or lower grade animal and adjust the value.
This is a concession (rukhsah) when the exact age is unavailable.
2
Understand the example
The commentator illustrates with bint makhad (1-year camel) and bint labun (2-year camel).
The value difference is typically 10 dirhams or two sheep.
3
Examine the proof
The hadith from Abu Bakr's letter shows that the Prophet commanded this practice.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
4
Note the compensation rules
When taking a higher grade, the collector returns the surplus; when taking a lower grade, the collector takes the deficit.
This ensures the zakat is of equal value.
5
Recognize the principle
Zakat can be collected by value (or substitute animal) when the exact age is unavailable.
This implies permissibility of cash valuation in zakat.

And Abu Yusuf said: Zakat is obligatory on them, one animal from them. [480] And from one upon whom a musinn (specific age) is obligatory and he does not have it, the collector takes a higher grade and returns the excess, or takes a lower grade and takes the excess. a: al-fisalan: plural of fasil, young camel. al-himlan: plural of himl, young sheep. al-ajajil: plural of majmul, young cow. [480] (7) For one upon whom a musinnah (specific age) is obligatory and he does not have it, the zakah collector takes a higher grade animal and returns the excess, or takes a lower grade and takes the excess. Example: If a one-year-old she-camel (bint makhad) was obligatory but the owner does not have bint makhad, but has a two-year-old she-camel (bint labun) whose value is generally 10 dirhams or two sheep more than bint makhad, the collector takes bint labun and returns the excess to the owner. The second scenario: the collector takes a lower grade than bint makhad and collects the difference in value from the owner so that the zakat is equal. And thus collecting zakat by value is permissible. Its proof is the hadith: that Abu Bakr wrote what Allah and His Messenger commanded: 'One whose zakat is due as bint makhad and he does not have it but has bint labun, it is accepted from him and the collector gives him 20 dirhams or two sheep. If he does not have bint makhad at all but has ibn labun, it is accepted from him and nothing is taken with it.' (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) Footnotes: ...
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on how to proceed when the exact zakat animal of the required age (musinn) is not available. The matn states that the zakah collector can take an animal of a higher grade and return the surplus value to the owner, or take a lower grade and collect the difference from the owner. The commentator illustrates with the example of bint makhad (1-year camel) and bint labun (2-year camel). The proof is the practice of Caliph Abu Bakr as recorded in a hadith. This ruling facilitates compliance: the owner need not procure the exact animal; substitution is allowed with monetary compensation. Implicitly, this also permits valuation in zakat (e.g., accepting cash or animals). The Hanafi position is that such substitution is valid; the mufta bihi is based on this hadith. Note: This applies only when the exact age is not available; if available, it must be given. Authority_weight: The hadith is from Sahih Bukhari, indicating strong evidence.

Key Terms
مسن (musinn): A specific age category of zakat animals (e.g., bint makhad, bint labun).
رد الفضل (radd al-faḍl): The collector returns the surplus value to the owner when taking a higher grade animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Hanafi school permits substituting a different age animal for zakat with monetary compensation, based on the practice of Abu Bakr.

Abu Yusuf's Ruling on Zakat for Young Animals
Abu Yusuf's ruling on zakat for young animals with proof from 'Ata.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Yusuf's ruling on zakat for young animals and identify the evidence he used.

Core Idea
Young animals at nisab alone incur zakat according to Abu Yusuf, based on an athar from 'Ata.

Imam Abu Yusuf departed from Abu Hanifa's position on zakat for young animals. While the relied-upon Hanafi view requires adult animals for nisab, Abu Yusuf argued that young animals alone, if they reach the nisab number, are zakatable. He supported his view with a narration from the tabi'i 'Ata Ibn Abi Rabah. This lesson unpacks his ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Recall that the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that zakat is not due on young animals unless they accompany adults. The nisab is counted from adults only.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that if young animals of a zakatable species (cows, sheep, goats, camels) reach the nisab number on their own, zakat is due on them, and the payment is one young animal from the herd.
E.g., 40 young sheep incur one young sheep as zakat.
3
Identify the proof
Abu Yusuf's proof is the athar from 'Ata, who affirmed that young sheep are counted for the owner. This is a direct textual evidence from a tabi'i.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Analyze the proof
Consider the strength of this proof: it is mursal (from a tabi'i directly), which Hanafis accept under conditions. It directly contradicts the principle of sa'imah that Abu Hanifa relied upon.
Hanafi usul accepts mursal hadith if supported by other evidence.
5
Determine the practical difference and tarjih
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Abu Yusuf, a person owning only young animals at nisab must pay zakat; under Abu Hanifa, no zakat is due. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The school's tarjih is based on the strength of the sa'imah principle and the mursal nature of the athar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۷۹] (۶) امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ان میں ایک بچہ لازم ہوگا۔ یعنی اگر تمیں گائے کے بچے ہوں تو ان میں ایک بچہ لازم ہوگا اس سے کم میں نہیں۔ کیونکہ اگر تمیں عدد سے کم بڑی گائیں ہوں تب بھی زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوتی تو چھوٹے بچے تمیں سے کم ہوں تو کیسے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ اسی طرح چالیس بکری کے بچے ہوں تو ان میں ایک بچہ لازم ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ بڑی بکری کا نصاب یہی ہے ۔ اور اگر بکری کے چالیس بچوں سے کم ہوں تو زکوۃ لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح پچھیں اونٹنی کے بچے ہوں تو ان میں ایک بچہ لازم ہو گا اس سے کم ہو تو لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
ے ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن عطاء قال قلت له يعتد بالصغار اولاد الشاة؟ قال نعم (الف ) مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۴ السخلة تحسب على صاحب الغنم - ج ثانی ص ۱۳۶۸ نمبر ۹۹۸۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بکری کے بچوں کا بھی شمار ہوگا اور اس کی زکوۃ لازم ہوگی۔
[479] (6) Imam Abu Yusuf said: One young animal is obligatory among them. Meaning, if you have young cows, then one young one is obligatory; less than that is not. Because if you have large cows less than the nisab, zakat is not obligatory; so if young ones are less than the nisab, how can zakat be obligatory? Similarly, if there are forty young sheep, one young one is obligatory, because the nisab for large sheep is that (forty). And if there are less than forty young sheep, zakat is not obligatory. Similarly, if there are five young she-camels, one young one is obligatory; less than that is not obligatory. And his proof is this narration: from 'Ata who said: I asked him: Are the young of sheep counted? He said: Yes. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 24: 'The lamb is counted for the owner of the sheep.' Vol. 2 p. 1368 no. 9983). From this narration it is understood that young sheep are counted and their zakat is obligatory.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This section presents the ruling of Imam Abu Yusuf regarding zakat on young animals. The passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute as it contrasts with the more widely held Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) that young animals are not counted for nisab unless they accompany adults. Abu Yusuf holds that if a person possesses only young animals of a zakatable species (cows, sheep, goats, camels) and they reach the nisab number (e.g., 30 cows, 40 sheep, 5 camels), then zakat is due on them, and the zakat payment is one young animal from that herd. He bases this on a narration from 'Ata Ibn Abi Rabah who affirms that young sheep are counted toward the nisab. The commentary explains the reasoning by analogy: just as adult animals below nisab incur no zakat, so too young animals below nisab incur none. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, who requires that the animals be pastoral (sa'imah) for zakat, and young animals are not considered pastoral until they reach a certain age; however, the text here is only presenting Abu Yusuf's view and its proof.

Key Terms
بچہ (bachcha): Young animal (calf, lamb, kid, camel calf).
نصاب (nisab): Minimum quantity of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.
اثر (athar): A narration from a Companion or early scholar, here from 'Ata.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, if a person owns 40 young sheep (sighar) and no adult sheep, what is the zakat due?
A) No zakat
B) One young sheep
C) One adult sheep
D) One-tenth of their value

Key Takeaway
Abu Yusuf's position on zakat for young animals is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is that young alone do not incur zakat.

Replacing Due Zakat Animal with Higher or Lower Grade
Ruling on substituting zakat animals with value adjustment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for substituting a zakat animal with a higher or lower grade and apply the value adjustment procedure.

Core Idea
When the exact zakat animal is unavailable, take a higher grade and refund the excess, or take a lower grade and collect the difference.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text addresses a practical problem: what happens if the owner does not have the exact animal prescribed for zakat? The Sharh al-Sameri provides a clear procedure based on prophetic instruction. By the end, you will understand the two permissible options and the basis for adjusting value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The owner is obligated to give a musinnah but does not have it. The zakat collector must act.
2
List the two options
Option 1: Take a higher grade animal and return the excess value. Option 2: Take a lower grade animal and collect the deficiency.
3
Understand the value adjustment
The excess/deficiency is calculated by market value or a standard like dirhams or sheep.
The text gives an example: bint makhāḍ vs bint labūn difference is 20 dirhams or two sheep.
4
Recognize the proof
The hadith of Abu Bakr records the Prophet's instruction, making this practice valid.
The hadith is ahad but accepted and applied by Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۰] ومن وجب عليه مسن فلم يوجد اخذ المصدق اعلى منها ورد الفضل او اخذ دونها واخذ الفضل. ا : الفصلان : فصیل کی جمع ہے اونٹنی کے بچے ۔ الحملان : حمل کی جمع ہے بکری کے بچے۔ العجا جیل : مجمول کی جمع ہے گائے کے بچے۔
[۴۸۰] (۷) کسی پر مسنہ واجب تھا اور مالک کے پاس منہ نہیں ہے تو زکوۃ لینے والا اس سے اعلی درجہ کا جانور لے اور جو زیادہ لیا اس کے روپے واپس کرے۔ یا مسنہ سے ادنی لے لے اور جو زیادہ ہوا مالک سے وہ لے لے۔ شرق مثلا ایک سال کی اونٹنی کا بچہ بنت مخاض لازم تھا لیکن مالک کے پاس بنت مخاض نہیں تھا البتہ دو سال کا بچہ بنت لبون تھا جس کی قیمت عموما بنت مخاض سے ہیں درہم زیادہ یا دو بکریاں زیادہ ہوتی تھی تو زکوۃ لینے والا مالک سے بنت لبون لے لے اور بنت مخاض سے جو زیادہ ہیں ہی در ہم آئے اس کو مالک کی طرف واپس کر دے۔ دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ بنت مخاض سے ادنی مالک لے لے اور بنت مخاض اور اس ادنی کے درمیان جو قیمت کا فرق ہے مثلا میں درہم یا دو بکریاں وہ بھی مالک سے وصول کرے تاکہ زکوۃ برابر سرابر ہو جائے ۔ اور اس طرح قیمت سے زکوۃ وصول کرنا جائز ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان ابـا بـكـر كتب له التي امر الله رسوله ومن بلغت صدقته بنت مخاض وليست عنده وعنده بنت لبون فانها تقبل منه ويعطيه المصدف عشرين درهما او شاتين فان لم يكن عنده بنت مخاض على وجهها و عنده ابن لبون فانه يقبل منه وليس معه شيء (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب العروض في الزکوۃ ص ۱۹۴ ۱۹۵ نمبر ۱۴۴۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب زکوۃ السائمۃ ص ۲۲۵ نمبر ۱۵۶۷، پہلی حدیث میں ہے ربخاری شریف ، باب من بلغت عنده صدقته
حاشیه : (الف) حضرت عطاء نے فرمایا میں نے پوچھا کیا بکری کے چھوٹے بچوں کو شمار کیا جائے گا؟ فرمایا ہاں ! (ب) حضرت ابو بکڑ نے وہ لکھا جس کا اللہ اور اس کے رسول نے حکم دیا تھا کہ جس کی زکوۃ بنت مخاض کو پہنچی ہو اور اس کے پاس بنت مخاض نہ ہو بلکہ اس کے پاس بنت لبون ہو تو وہ قبول کر لیا جائے گا اور زکوۃ لینے والا مالک کو میں درہم واپس دے گا یا دو بکریاں دے گا۔ اور اگر اس کے پاس بنت مخاض اس طرح کا نہ ہو بلکہ ابن لیون ہو تو اس کو قبول کر لیا جائے گا اور اس کے ساتھ کچھ نہیں ہوگا۔
[480] Whoever is obligated to pay a musinnah (a camel of a specific age) and does not have it, the zakah collector takes a higher grade and returns the excess (value), or takes a lower grade and collects the excess. Explanation: al-faslān is the plural of fasīl meaning young camel; al-ḥamlān is plural of ḥaml meaning young sheep; al-‘ajājīl is plural of ‘ajjūl meaning young cow. (7) If someone owes a musinnah but the owner does not have it, the zakah collector takes an animal of a higher grade and returns the extra money, or takes a lower grade and collects the extra. For example, if a bint makhāḍ (one-year-old she-camel) is due but the owner does not have it, but he has a bint labūn (two-year-old she-camel) whose value is usually ten dirhams or two sheep more than a bint makhāḍ, then the zakah collector takes the bint labūn and returns the excess (the ten dirhams) to the owner. The other case is that he takes a lower grade animal and collects the difference in value from the owner so that the zakat becomes equal. And taking zakat by value in this manner is permissible. Its proof is the hadith: 'Abu Bakr wrote what the Prophet (SAW) commanded: Whoever's zakat is due as bint makhāḍ and he does not have it but has bint labūn, it is accepted from him, and the zakah collector gives him twenty dirhams or two sheep. And if he does not have bint makhāḍ exactly but has ibn labūn, it is accepted from him and nothing extra is taken.' (Bukhari, Bab al-‘Urūḍ fī al-Zakāh, p. 194-195 no. 1448; Abu Dawud, Bāb Zakāh al-Sā’imah p. 225 no. 1567).
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling when the exact animal due as zakat (e.g., a specific age and type of camel) is not available. The zakah collector has two options: take a higher grade animal and refund the price difference to the owner, or take a lower grade animal and collect the difference from the owner. The commentator explains with an example: if bint makhāḍ is due but only bint labūn is available (which is more valuable), the collector takes the bint labūn and gives back the extra value (e.g., ten dirhams or two sheep). Alternatively, if a lower grade animal is taken, the owner must pay the difference. This practice is justified by the hadith of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, which records the Prophet's instruction. The hadith also shows that accepting value (qīmah) in lieu of the specific animal is valid, as the collector gives dirhams or sheep to equalize the value.

Key Terms
مسن (musinn): A camel of a specific age due as zakat (e.g., bint makhāḍ, bint labūn).
مصدق (musaddiq): Zakah collector appointed by the state.
فضل (fadl): Excess value or amount given or taken to equalize the zakat payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Reject the bint labūn and demand the exact bint makhāḍ
B) Take the bint labūn and return the extra value to the owner
C) Take only cash equal to the value of bint makhāḍ
D) Take the bint labūn without any compensation

Key Takeaway
When the exact zakat animal is unavailable, the collector may take a higher or lower grade substitute and adjust the value, based on prophetic instruction.

Permissibility of Paying Value (Qīmah) in Zakat
Ruling that paying the market value is permissible in zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that paying value in zakat is permissible and identify the evidence from the practice of Mu'adh.

Core Idea
You may pay the cash value of a zakatable item instead of the item itself.

Many assume zakat must always be paid in kind—grain for grain, livestock for livestock. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that paying the market value (qīmah) is permissible, based on a clear precedent from the Companion Mu'adh. Understanding this ruling makes zakat easier and more practical in modern economies.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the central ruling: paying value (qīmah) in zakat is permissible (ja'iz). Note that this is not an obligation; one may still give the specific item.
The ruling is categorized as permissible (mubah), not obligatory.
2
Locate the evidence
The text cites two proofs: a previous hadith (from Abu Bakr, referenced earlier) and the action of Mu'adh. Focus on Mu'adh's statement to the people of Yemen.
Mu'adh's action is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Mu'adh asked for clothes (thiyāb) instead of barley and millet. This substitution shows that the Companions understood zakat as an obligation of value, not of specific physical items.
The principle is called qīmah – equivalent monetary value.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (especially Shafi'i) contest this view. They argue that zakat must be given exactly as prescribed (e.g., sheep for sheep).
This is a legitimate scholarly difference.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the practice of the Companions and istihsan (juristic preference) to uphold the permissibility of qīmah. This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling is based on need and ease for the payer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۱] (۸) ويجوز دفع القيم فى الزکوة [۴۸۱] (۸) زکوۃ میں چیز کی قیمت دینا جائز ہے۔
اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبرے میں گزرگئی ہے۔
(۲) ایک اثر سے بھی اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ قال معاذ لاهل اليمن ائتوني بعرض ثياب خميص او لبيس في الصدقة مكان الشعير والذرة اهون عليكم وخير لاصحاب النبي الله الله بالمدينة (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب العروض فى الزکوۃ ص۱۹۴ نمبر ۱۴۴۸) اس اثر میں حضرت معاذ نے جو اور باجرے کے بدلے میں کپڑے لئے ہیں۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو چیز واجب ہو اس کی قیمت لگا کر دوسری چیز یا روپیہ لے سکتے ہیں۔
[481] (8) And it is permissible to pay the value (qīmah) in zakat. (8) Paying the price of the item in zakat is permissible. Its proof has passed in the previous issue. (2) Another narration supports it: Mu'adh said to the people of Yemen: 'Bring me a display of clothes, khamees or labis, as sadaqah instead of barley and millet. It is easier for you and better for the Companions of the Prophet in Madinah.' (Bukhari, Bab al-‘Urūḍ fī al-Zakāh, p. 194 no. 1448). In this narration, Mu'adh took clothes in exchange for wheat and barley, showing that one can set a value for the due item and take another item or money.

Commentary
This section explicitly states the permissibility of giving the monetary value (qīmah) instead of the specific zakatable item. The commentator refers to the previous proof (hadith of Abu Bakr) and adds supporting evidence from the action of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, who collected clothes from the people of Yemen instead of the prescribed grains. This demonstrates that the principle of substituting value is recognized in early practice. In Hanafi fiqh, this is the relied-upon position, allowing zakat to be paid in cash or equivalent value, which facilitates the payment.

Key Terms
قيم (qīmah): Monetary value or equivalent price of the zakatable item.
عرض ('arḍ): Trade goods or commodities (here: clothes).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Exemption of Working, Draft, and Fed Animals from Zakat
Ruling on exemption of working, draft, and fed animals from zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of animals exempt from zakat in Hanafi fiqh and prove the exemption using hadith, athar, and qiyas.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock is only for sa'imah animals; working and fed animals are exempt.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam, but not all wealth is subject to it. The Hanafi school specifies that zakat on livestock applies only to grazing (sa'imah) animals. In this lesson, we examine the clear exemptions: animals used for work, for carrying loads, and those fed at home. The evidence comes from the Prophet's ﷺ hadith and the practice of the early Muslims, with reasoning extended by qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three exempt categories
From the text, note the three Arabic terms: 'awāmil (working), ḥawāmil (draft), ‘ulūfah (fed at home). Understand that these are not sa'imah (grazing).
'Ulūfah refers to animals fed from the owner's property for most of the year.
2
Examine the primary dalil for 'awāmil
The hadith from Ali (ra) states 'there is nothing on working animals' (laysa 'alā al-'awāmil shay'). Identify this as the direct proof for exemption of working animals.
The hadith is in Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan al-Daraqutni; its transmission is zanni but meaning is clear.
3
Examine the dalil for 'ulūfah
The athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i exempts sheep raised fed at home (ghanam al-rabā'ib). Then the commentator extends this by qiyas to other species.
The illa for qiyas is that the animal is not sa'imah; it does not graze freely, so wealth is not increasing.
4
Synthesize the underlying principle
Combine the evidence: zakat on livestock is conditioned on the animal being sa'imah. Therefore, any animal that is not sa'imah—be it working, draft, or fed—is exempt.
This principle is consistent with the general rule that zakat is on naturally increasing wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۲] (۹) وليس في العوامل والحوامل والعلوفة زكوة [۴۸۲] (۹) کام کرنے والے بوجھ اٹھانے والے اور گھر پر کھانے والے جانوروں میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ وہ جانور جو گھر میں کام کرنے کے لئے ہوں یا بوجھ اٹھانے کے لئے ہوں ان میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن علی قال زهير احسبه عن النبي الله ... وليس على العوامل شیء (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب زکوۃ السائمته ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۵۷۲ مردار قطنی لیس فی العوامل صدقہ ج ثانی ص ۸۸ نمبر ۱۹۲۱ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کام کرنے والے جانور میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ اور علوفہ یعنی سال کے زیادہ مہنوں میں گھر پر کھا کر زندگی گزارتے ہوں ان پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل بی اثر ہے عن ابراهيم قال ليس في غنم الربائب صدقة (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۳ في الرجل تکون لہ الغنم في المصر سخت کھاج ثانی، جس نے ۳۶ نمبر (۹۹۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس بکری کو گھر میں کھلا کر پالتے ہوں اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی پر قیاس کر کے دوسرے جانوروں میں بھی جن کو گھر میں کھلا کر پال رہا ہے اس سے بھی مال بڑھ نہیں رہا ہے بلکہ مالک کا مال جانور میں شامل ہو رہا ہے اس لئے اس میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ زکوۃ والی حدیث میں ہر جگہ سائمہ کا لفظ گزرا اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ چرنے والے جانور میں زکوۃ ہے۔ گھر پر کھانے والے جانور میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔
[482] (9) And there is no zakat on working animals, draft animals, and animals fed at home. (9) Animals used for work, carrying loads, and those fed at home (not grazing) have no zakat. Its proof is the hadith from 'Ali, narrated by Zuhayr (I think) from the Prophet (SAW): 'And there is nothing on working animals.' (Abu Dawud, Bab Zakāh al-Sā’imah, p. 228 no. 1572; al-Daraqutni: 'There is no sadaqah on working animals,' vol. 2 p. 88 no. 1921). From this hadith it is clear that working animals have no zakat. As for 'ulūfah (animals that are fed at home for most of the year), there is no zakat on them. Its proof is the narration from Ibrahim: 'There is no sadaqah on sheep that are raised fed at home (ghanam al-rabā’ib).' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 9986). From this narration it is clear that sheep fed at home have no zakat. By qiyas, the same applies to other animals fed at home, because wealth is not increasing; rather the owner's wealth is being consumed by the animal, so no zakat. In the hadiths of zakat, the word sā'imah (grazing) is used everywhere, so it indicates that zakat is on grazing animals, not on animals fed at home.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This section establishes the exemption from zakat for three categories of animals: (1) 'awāmil (working animals, e.g., oxen used for plowing), (2) ḥawāmil (draft animals, e.g., donkeys used for carrying loads), and (3) ‘ulūfah (animals fed at home, i.e., not grazing freely in the pasture for most of the year). The proof for working animals is a hadith from ‘Ali (ra) that there is no zakat on them. For fed animals, the commentary cites an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i that sheep raised at home (ghanam al-rabā’ib) are not subject to zakat. The commentator then applies qiyas to other species. The underlying principle is that zakat is only on sā'imah (grazing) livestock because zakat is prescribed on wealth that naturally increases; animals that are fed at home actually consume the owner's wealth rather than increase it. This is a fundamental rule in Hanafi zakat law.

Key Terms
عوامل ('awāmil): Animals used for work (plowing, pulling).
حوامل (ḥawāmil): Animals used for carrying loads (draft animals).
علوفة ('ulūfah): Animals that are fed at home (not grazing freely).
سائمه (sā'imah): Grazing livestock that pasture freely for most of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) An ox used for plowing the fields
C) Camels kept for milk and grazing freely
D) Goats that graze in the desert

Key Takeaway
Zakat on livestock is only due on sa'imah (grazing) animals; working, draft, and fed animals are exempt.

Paying Value in Zakat is Permissible
Ruling with proof that paying value in zakat is allowed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on paying value in zakat and identify the proofs from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Paying the market value of the obligatory animal in zakat is permissible in the Hanafi school.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam, but what if the specific item owed is unavailable? The Hanafi school provides flexibility by allowing the payer to give the market value instead. This lesson examines the ruling and the evidence from the sunnah that supports it, including the famous hadith of Mu'adh (ra) accepting clothes in place of barley and corn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage states clearly: 'Paying the value in zakat is permissible.' Recognize that this is the Hanafi position.
The hukm level is mubah (permissible), but with a stronger recommendation when it facilitates payment.
2
Locate the Dalil
Two proofs are given: (1) The hadith about bint makhad and bint labun, where compensation is given; (2) The athar of Mu'adh taking clothes instead of grains.
Both are from Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith shows that when the exact animal is absent, a substitute with compensation is accepted, implying that value can replace the obligatory item. The athar explicitly demonstrates taking clothes (value) instead of the owed grains.
This is how the Hanafi school derives permissibility.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not permit paying value; they require the specific item (or equivalent in kind).
The disagreement is based on differing usul principles regarding 'from the property itself'.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, from Zahir al-Riwayah, and is considered stronger due to the clear practice of a Companion.
The rule of 'necessity brings ease' also supports this.

Source Text

ويجوز دفع القيم فى الزكوة
بنت مخاض وليست عنده ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۱۳۵۳)) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مالک پر بنت مخاض لازم ہو اور اس کے پاس بنت مخاض نہ ہو تو اس سے بنت لبون لے لے اور زکوۃ لینے والا مالک کو بیس درہم دے یا دو بکریاں دیدے تاکہ بنت مخاض گویا کہ ہو جائے ۔ اس حدیث سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ جو جانور واجب ہوا ہو اس کے بدلے میں اس کی قیمت بھی دے سکتے ہیں (۲) ایک اثر سے بھی اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ قال معاذ لاهل اليمن ائتوني بعرض ثياب خميص او لبيس في الصدقة مكان الشعير والذرة اهون عليكم وخير لاصحاب النبي الله الله بالمدينة (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب العروض فى الزکوۃ ص۱۹۴ نمبر ۱۴۴۸) اس اثر میں حضرت معاذ نے جو اور باجرے کے بدلے میں کپڑے لئے ہیں۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو چیز واجب ہو اس کی قیمت لگا کر دوسری چیز یا روپیہ لے سکتے ہیں۔
المصدق : زکوة لینے والا، الفضل : جو قیمت زیادہ ہو۔
[۴۸۱] (۸) زکوۃ میں چیز کی قیمت دینا جائز ہے۔
اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبرے میں گزرگئی ہے۔
It is permissible to pay the value in zakat. From the hadith (bint makhad not in his possession...) it is understood that the owner is required to give a bint makhad, and if he does not have it, then accept a bint labun and the zakat collector gives him twenty dirhams or two goats so that it becomes as if it were a bint makhad. From this hadith it is also understood that if an animal is obligatory, one can pay its value instead. (2) This is also supported by an athar: Mu'adh said to the people of Yemen: 'Bring me clothes, khumays or labis, in charity instead of barley and corn, which is easier for you and better for the companions of the Prophet in Medina.' In this athar, Mu'adh took clothes instead of barley and corn, showing that one can evaluate the obligatory item and take another thing or money. Al-musaddiq: the zakat collector; al-fadl: the extra value. [481] (8) Paying the value of the item in zakat is permissible. Its evidence has passed in the earlier issue.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that it is permissible to pay the market value (qimah) of the obligatory animal in zakat instead of the specific animal. The text opens with the concise ruling, then provides two proofs: (1) A hadith about bint makhad and bint labun, where the zakat collector can accept a higher-age animal and give compensation, indicating that value can substitute for the exact required item. (2) The famous athar of Mu'adh (ra) where he accepted clothes from the people of Yemen instead of grains, proving that the value of the obligatory item can be taken. The commentary defines key terms: al-musaddiq (zakat collector) and al-fadl (excess value). The ruling is repeated at the end for emphasis. This is the established Hanafi position, known from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
قيم (qimah): The market value of the obligatory commodity, which can be paid in zakat instead of the specific animal.
بنت مخاض (bint makhad): A one-year-old female camel, the minimum age for zakat on camels.
بنت لبون (bint labun): A two-year-old female camel, taken when a bint makhad is not available.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not permissible; the exact item must be given.
B) It is permissible, as shown by the hadith of Mu'adh.
C) It is permissible only for camels and goats.
D) It is permissible only if the zakat collector agrees.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, paying the market value of the obligatory zakat item is permissible, supported by the hadith of bint makhad and the practice of Mu'adh (ra).
