Zakat Collector Takes Middle Quality
Ruling that the zakat collector must take the average quality, not the best or worst

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the zakat collector must take the average quality and cite the prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
Justice in zakat: the collector must take the average—neither the best nor the worst.

This lesson addresses a specific duty of the zakat collector: what quality of property must be taken when collecting zakat? The Shariah mandates a middle path to balance the rights of the payer and the poor. Two hadiths provide clear guidance, and the Hanafi school enforces this as wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the zakat collector's choice of quality when taking zakat from livestock or wealth. The ruling: it is wajib to take the average quality, not the best or the worst.
The ruling applies to all zakatable items.
2
Locate the dalil
Two prophetic hadiths are cited: (1) The letter of Abu Bakr (ra) prohibits taking aged, defective, or a breeding male goat except by the collector's discretion. (2) The Prophet (ﷺ) told Mu'adh (ra) when sending him to Yemen to avoid the best of people's wealth.
Both hadiths are authentic (Bukhari).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of taking the best (karaim) and the worst (herma, dhat 'awar) implies that only the middle quality remains acceptable. The phrase 'except what the collector wishes' does not permit arbitrary choice but refers to discretion within the average.
The evidence is from the Sunnah (ahad) but its meaning is clear.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
All schools agree on the principle of taking the average. Differences may exist on what constitutes 'best' or 'worst' in specific contexts.
No major inter-madhhab dispute on this ruling.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
The collector must take the average quality. Taking the best is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) because it overburdens the payer; taking the worst harms the poor. The mufta bihi is wajib to take middle.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۳] (۱۰) ولا يأخذ المصدق خيارا المال ولا رذالته و يأخذ الوسط
(۱) یہ شریعت کا انصاف ہے کہ نہ اعلی درجے کا مال لے اور نہ گھٹیا درجے کا بلکہ اوسط درجے کا مال لے(۲) ان انسا حدثه ان ابا بكر كتب له التي امر الله رسوله الا الله ولا يخرج في الصدقة هرمة ولا ذات عوار ولا تيس الا ماشاء المصدق (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب لایو خذ فى الصدقة هرمة ولا ذات عوار ولا تمیں الا ماشاء المصدق ص ۱۹۶ نمبر ۱۴۵۵ را بو داؤد شریف، باب زکوۃ السائمة ص ۲۲۶ نمبر ۱۵۷۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعلی اور ادنی مال نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ بلکہ اوسط جانور لیا جائے گا (۲) عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله الا الله لما بعث معاذ على اليمن .... وتوق كرائم اموال الناس (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب لا تؤ خذکر ائم اموال الناس فی الصدقی ص ۹۶ نمبر ۱۴۵۸) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ لینے والا اچھا اور اعلی درجہ کا مال نہ لے۔
[483] (10) The zakat collector shall not take the best of the wealth nor the worst, but shall take the middle. (1) This is the justice of the Shariah: neither the best quality nor the worst, but the middle. (2) Anas (ra) narrated that Abu Bakr (ra) wrote for him what Allah commanded His Messenger: 'Do not take in charity an aged animal, nor one with a defect, nor a he-goat, except what the zakat collector wishes.' (a) (Bukhari, Bab La Yu'khadh fi al-Sadaqah Hirmah...) This hadith shows that the best and the worst are not taken, but the middle animal. (2) From Ibn Abbas (ra) that when the Prophet (ﷺ) sent Mu'adh to Yemen... 'and avoid the best of people's wealth.' (b) (Bukhari, Bab La Tu'khadh Karaim Amwal al-Nas) This hadith also shows that the zakat collector should not take good and high-quality wealth.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi principle of justice in zakat collection: the collector must take the average quality of the livestock or wealth, neither the best nor the worst. Two proofs are cited: (1) The letter of Abu Bakr (ra) attributed to the Prophet (ﷺ), which forbids taking aged, defective, or breeding males except by the collector's discretion, implying avoidance of extremes. (2) The Prophet's instruction to Mu'adh (ra) to avoid the 'best of people's wealth.' This ensures fairness: the payer is not burdened by giving his best property, and the poor receive adequate quality. The ruling applies to all zakatable items.

Key Terms
خيار المال (khiyar al-mal): The best quality of property; the zakat collector should not take this.
رذالة المال (rudhalah al-mal): The worst quality of property; also not to be taken.
الوسط (al-wasat): The middle, average quality; what the collector must take.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Take the middle quality, neither the best nor the worst.
D) Take any quality as per the collector's discretion.

Key Takeaway
The zakat collector must take the average quality of wealth, as mandated by the Sunnah, to ensure justice for both giver and recipient.

Adding New Property of Same Type During the Zakat Year
Ruling and proof for adding mal mustafad of same type to existing nisab for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on mal mustafad by combining it with existing nisab of the same type and paying zakat at the end of the original year.

Core Idea
New property of the same type is added to existing nisab; zakat is paid on the total at year-end without a separate haul.

This passage introduces the Hanafi rule for zakat on mal mustafad (newly acquired wealth) when it belongs to the same category as an existing nisab. The ruling simplifies zakat calculation by allowing combination, based on the practice of al-Zuhri. Understanding this principle is essential for accurate zakat fulfillment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the existing nisab and its type (jins)
Determine the type of wealth you already possess (e.g., cows, gold, silver, cash, trade goods) and confirm it reaches nisab at the start of the year.
2
Check if new property is of the same type
Any additional wealth acquired during the year (mal mustafad) must be classified by type. If it matches the existing nisab's jins, proceed to combination.
Same type means same zakati category: all cows, all gold, all cash, etc.
3
Combine and pay zakat at year-end
Add the mustafad amount to the existing nisab. Pay zakat on the total at the end of the original haul (when the original nisab completes its year).
The new portion does not need its own year; the original year suffices.
4
Recognize the exception: different type
If the acquired property is of a different type (e.g., gold when you have silver), it cannot be combined. That new wealth must complete its own separate year before zakat is due.
This exception is implied in the source text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۴] (١١) ومن كان له نصابا فاستفاد فى اثناء الحول من جنسه ضمه الى ماله وزكاه به.
مثلا چالیس گائے موجود ہیں جو گائے کا نصاب ہے اور درمیان سال میں گائے کے ہیں بچھڑے ہوئے اب چالیس گایوں کی زکوۃ نصاب میں دینا تھی لیکن ہیں بچھڑوں پر سال پورا نہیں ہوتا صرف چھ ماہ ہوتے ہیں تو ان میں بچھڑوں کو بھی چالیس گانوں کے ساتھ ملا کر رمضان میں ساٹھ گالیوں کی زکوۃ دے۔ چاہے ہیں بچھڑوں پر سال نہ گزرا ہو۔
یہ نہیں بچھڑے درمیان سال میں مال مستفاد ہیں۔ اور اس کی جنس بھی وہی ہے جو مال نصاب پہلے سے ہے یعنی گائے اس لئے دونوں کی زکوۃ رمضان میں ادا کرے (۲) اثر میں موجود ہے عن الزهرى انه كان يقول اذا استفاد الرجل ما لا فاراد ان ينفقه قبل مجيء شهر زكوته فليز كه ثم لينفقه وان كان لا يريد ان ينفق فليز كه مع ماله ( ج ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۴۹ من قال یزکیہ اذا استفاده ج ثانی ص ۱۳۸۷ نمبر ۱۰۲۲۷ار مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب وجوب الصدقة في الحول ج رابع ص ۳۲ نمبر ۶۸۷۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال مستفاد میں مال نصاب کے ساتھ زکوۃ واجب ہے۔
و اگر نصاب کے علاوہ کوئی مال درمیان میں مستفاد ہوا تو اس پر سال گزرنے کے بعد ہی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت انس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت ابو بکر نے لکھا جس کا اللہ نے اس کے رسول کو حکم دیا ہے کہ زکوۃ میں بوڑھا اور اندھا نہ نکالے اور نہ سانڈ کو نکالے مگر جو ز کوۃ لینے والے چاہے (ب) حضور نے جب حضرت معاذ کو یمن روانہ فرمایا تو فرمایا لوگوں کے اعلی مال سے بچتے رہو (ج) حضرت زھری فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ آدمی مال کا استفادہ کرے پھر ارادہ کرے کہ زکوۃ کا مہینہ آنے سے پہلے خرچ کرے تو اس کی زکوۃ دے پھر خرچ کرے اور اگر خرچ کرنا نہیں چاہتا ہے تو اپنے مال کے ساتھ مستفاد کی بھی مزکوۃ دے۔
[484] (11) Whoever has a nisab and then acquires during the year property of the same type, he adds it to his wealth and gives zakat on it. For example, forty cows exist, which is the nisab of cows, and in the middle of the year calves are born from cows. Now, the zakat of forty cows was due at the completion of the nisab, but the calves have not completed a full year, only six months. So he adds the calves to the forty cows and gives zakat of sixty cows in Ramadan, even if the calves have not completed a year. These calves are acquired property (mal mustafad) mid-year, and their type is the same as the existing nisab, i.e., cows, so he gives zakat of both in Ramadan. (2) There is an athar from al-Zuhri that he used to say: 'If a man acquires wealth and wants to spend it before the arrival of the month of his zakat, he should give zakat on it and then spend it. And if he does not want to spend it, he should give zakat on it together with his wealth.' (c) (Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) This athar shows that zakat is obligatory on acquired (mustafad) wealth along with the nisab. If someone acquires wealth other than the nisab during the year, zakat is due only after a full year passes. Footnotes: (a) Anas said that Abu Bakr wrote... (b) The Prophet said to Mu'adh: 'Avoid the best of people's wealth.' (c) al-Zuhri used to say: 'If a man acquires wealth and intends...'
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This lesson covers the Hanafi ruling on mal mustafad (newly acquired property) of the same type as an existing nisab. The principle: if one already possesses a nisab (e.g., 40 cows) and acquires more of the same kind (e.g., calves) mid-year, the new property is added to the existing stock, and zakat is paid on the total at the end of the original year, regardless of whether the new property has completed a full year of its own. The example clarifies: if 40 cows (nisab) produce calves after six months, at year's end zakat is due on 60 cows (40 + 20 calves) even though the calves only existed for six months. The proof is an athar from al-Zuhri confirming that mustafad wealth is combined with existing nisab for zakat. An important exception is noted: if the acquired property is of a different type (not the same jins), it does not combine and must complete its own year. The footnotes (a) and (b) are from the previous lesson's hadiths and are included here inadvertently.

Key Terms
مال مستفاد (mal mustafad): Newly acquired property that comes into one's possession during the zakat year.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.
الحول (al-hawl): The lunar year that must pass for zakat to become due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on zakat for a person who has 40 cows and acquires 10 more cows during the year?
A) Zakat is due only on the original 40 cows at year end.
B) The 10 new cows must complete their own year before zakat is due.
C) At year end, zakat is due on all 50 cows together.
D) Zakat must be paid immediately on the new cows upon acquisition.

Key Takeaway
Mal mustafad of the same type as existing nisab is combined for zakat calculation; no separate haul required.

Zakat on Acquired Wealth: The Case of Same-Type Additions
Ruling on adding acquired wealth to existing nisab for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mal mustafad of the same type, identify the Shafi'i counterargument, and explain why the year of the original nisab suffices.

Core Idea
Same-type wealth acquired mid-year joins the nisab's year; zakat is due on the total at the end.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: you already have a nisab (e.g., 40 cows), and during the year you acquire more of the same type (e.g., calves born). Does each new addition start its own zakat year? The Hanafi school says no—it is added to the existing nisab. The Shafi'i school disagrees. We will work through the ruling, the proofs, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What is the act? Zakat on acquired wealth (mal mustafad). What exactly is disputed: whether a separate year is required for the acquired wealth.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
The matn rules: add to existing wealth and pay zakat on the total at the end of the original year. Evidence: athar from Zuhri and the principle that the year of the nisab covers additions of the same type.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Shafi'i: each portion of wealth requires a full year. Proof: hadith from Ibn Umar, 'Whoever acquires wealth, no zakat is due until a year passes.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response: the hadith applies when there is no pre-existing nisab. With a pre-existing nisab, the year of the nisab covers the acquired wealth of the same type.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if someone has 40 cows and gets 10 more mid-year, Hanafi pays zakat on 50 at year-end; Shafi'i pays on only 40 until the 10 complete their year.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۴](١١) ومن كان له نصابا فاستفاد فى اثناء الحول من جنسه ضمه الى ماله وزكاه به. کو گھر میں کھلا کر پالا جاتا ہو۔
[۴۸۴] (۱۱) جس کے پاس نصاب کا مال ہو پھر سال کے درمیان میں اسی نصاب کی جنس سے فائدہ حاصل کیا تو اس کو مال کے ساتھ ملائے گا اور اس کی زکوۃ دے گا۔
مثلا چالیس گائے موجود ہیں جو گائے کا نصاب ہے اور درمیان سال میں گائے کے ہیں بچھڑے ہوئے اب چالیس گایوں کی زکوۃ نصاب میں دینا تھی لیکن ہیں بچھڑوں پر سال پورا نہیں ہوتا صرف چھ ماہ ہوتے ہیں تو ان میں بچھڑوں کو بھی چالیس گانوں کے ساتھ ملا کر رمضان میں ساٹھ گالیوں کی زکوۃ دے۔ چاہے ہیں بچھڑوں پر سال نہ گزرا ہو۔
یہ نہیں بچھڑے درمیان سال میں مال مستفاد ہیں۔ اور اس کی جنس بھی وہی ہے جو مال نصاب پہلے سے ہے یعنی گائے اس لئے دونوں کی زکوۃ رمضان میں ادا کرے (۲) اثر میں موجود ہے عن الزهرى انه كان يقول اذا استفاد الرجل ما لا فاراد ان ينفقه قبل مجيء شهر زكوته فليز كه ثم لينفقه وان كان لا يريد ان ينفق فليز كه مع ماله ( ج ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ ۴۹ من قال یزکیہ اذا استفاده ج ثانی ص ۱۳۸۷ نمبر ۱۰۲۲۷ار مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب وجوب الصدقة في الحول ج رابع ص ۳۲ نمبر ۶۸۷۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مال مستفاد میں مال نصاب کے ساتھ زکوۃ واجب ہے۔
و اگر نصاب کے علاوہ کوئی مال درمیان میں مستفاد ہوا تو اس پر سال گزرنے کے بعد ہی زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت انس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت ابو بکر نے لکھا جس کا اللہ نے اس کے رسول کو حکم دیا ہے کہ زکوۃ میں بوڑھا اور اندھا نہ نکالے اور نہ سانڈ کو نکالے مگر جو ز کوۃ لینے والے چاہے (ب) حضور نے جب حضرت معاذ کو یمن روانہ فرمایا تو فرمایا لوگوں کے اعلی مال سے بچتے رہو (ج) حضرت زھری فرمایا کرتے تھے کہ آدمی مال کا استفادہ کرے پھر ارادہ کرے کہ زکوۃ کا مہینہ آنے سے پہلے خرچ کرے تو اس کی زکوۃ دے پھر خرچ کرے اور اگر خرچ کرنا نہیں چاہتا ہے تو اپنے مال کے ساتھ مستفاد کی بھی مزکوۃ دے۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل)
۳۱۴
كتاب الزكوة
[۴۸۵] (۱۲) والسائمة هى التى تكتفى بالرعى فى اكثر الحول فان علفها نصف الحول او اكثر فلا زكوة فيها [۱۳۴۸۲) والزكوة عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف في النصاب انده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب تک مال مستفاد پر سال نہ گزر جائے زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الا الله من استفاد مالا فلا زكوة عليه حتى يحول عليه الحول (الف) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء لا زکوۃ
على المال المستفاد حتی حال علیہ الحول ص ۱۳۷ نمبر ۶۳۱ دار قطنی ، باب وجوب الزكوة بالحول ج ثانی ص سے لے نمبر۱۸۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک خود مال مستفاد پر سال نہ گزر جائے اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
(11) Whoever has a nisab and then acquires during the year from the same type, he adds it to his wealth and gives zakat on it. (He keeps it open in the house to be raised.) (11) The one who has nisab wealth, then during the year he acquires profit from the same type of the nisab, he will add it to the wealth and give its zakat. For example: forty cows are present, which is the nisab of cows, and during the year calves are born. Now zakat was due on forty cows, but the calves have not completed a year, only six months. So he will add the calves to the forty cows and give zakat on sixty cows in Ramadan, even though the calves have not completed a year. These calves are mal mustafad acquired during the year, and their type is the same as the pre-existing nisab (cows), so he will pay zakat on both in Ramadan. (2) In the athar: from Zuhri that he used to say: If a man acquires wealth and intends to spend it before the month of its zakat comes, then let him give zakat on it and then spend it. And if he does not intend to spend, then let him give zakat on it with his wealth. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). From this athar it is known that zakat is wajib on mal mustafad together with the nisab. And if wealth other than the nisab is acquired mid-year, then zakat will be wajib only after the passage of a year. Footnote: (a) Anas narrates that Abu Bakr wrote that which Allah commanded His Messenger: do not take old or blind in zakat, nor a bull, except what the collector wishes. (b) The Prophet when sending Mu'adh to Yemen said: stay away from people's best wealth. (c) Zuhri used to say: if a man acquires wealth and intends to spend before the zakat month, then give zakat on it and then spend; if not, then give zakat on the acquired together with his wealth. Page 319: ... And Imam Shafi'i says: zakat is not wajib on mal mustafad until a year passes. His proof is the hadith: from Ibn Umar that the Prophet said: whoever acquires wealth, there is no zakat on him until a year passes over it. (Tirmidhi, Dar Qutni). From this hadith it is known that until a year passes over the mal mustafad itself, zakat is not wajib on it.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage covers the Hanafi ruling on mal mustafad (wealth acquired during the zakat year). The matn states that if one already has a nisab and acquires more of the same type during the year, he adds it to his existing wealth and pays zakat on the total at the end of the year. The commentary gives the example of cows: if one has 40 cows (nisab) and then calves are born, he pays zakat on all 60 cows at the end of the year, even though the calves have not completed a year. The evidence includes an athar from Zuhri. The Shafi'i position is then presented: they require a full year for the acquired wealth itself. The Hanafi position relies on the principle that the year of the original nisab covers the acquired wealth if of the same type. The Shafi'i proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar. This is a clear inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi school views the year of the original nisab as sufficient for the new addition.

Key Terms
مال مستفاد (mal mustafad): Wealth acquired during the zakat year, either from profit or new acquisition.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone already has 40 cows (nisab) and acquires 10 more cows during the year, when is zakat due on those 10?
A) After a full year from the date of acquisition
B) At the end of the original year along with the 40
C) Never, because they are born during the year
D) Only if they exceed the nisab on their own

Key Takeaway
Same-type acquired wealth does not start a new zakat year; it joins the existing nisab's year.

Definition of Sa'imah and Zakat on Grazing Livestock
Defining sa'imah and deriving the zakat exclusion for fed livestock

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sa'imah and 'ulufah, state the condition for zakat on livestock, and apply the Hanafi ruling that only grazing livestock are subject to zakat.

Core Idea
Only livestock that graze for most of the year are subject to zakat; fodder-fed animals are exempt.

This passage defines the key term sa'imah (grazing livestock) and establishes a critical distinction for zakat: only animals that depend on natural pasture for the majority of the year are zakatable. The Hanafi school relies on a hadith specifying 'sa'imah' to exempt fodder-fed animals ('ulufah). Understanding this distinction prevents incorrect zakat calculations.

Guided Path
1
State the definition
Identify what makes an animal sa'imah according to the text: it suffices with grazing for most of the year.
2
Identify the threshold
Note the quantitative condition: grazing must be for 'most of the year' (akthar al-hawl), meaning more than half, i.e., >6 months.
3
Contrast the opposite
Understand 'ulufah: if fed for half the year or more, the animal is not sa'imah and no zakat is due.
4
Connect to the proof
Recognize that the hadith specifies 'sa'imah', making the ruling conditional on grazing status.
Hadith: '...if a man's sa'imah is less than forty sheep...'
5
Apply the ruling
Determine whether a given herd is subject to zakat based on the grazing period relative to the threshold.

Source Text

[۴۸۵] (۱۲) والسائمة هى التى تكتفى بالرعى فى اكثر الحول فان علفها نصف الحول او اكثر فلا زكوة فيها
[۴۸۵] (۱۲) سائمہ، چرنے والے جانوران کو کہتے ہیں کہ وہ سال کے اکثر حصہ میں چرنے پر اکتفا کرے، پس اگر جانور کو آدھا سال یا زیادہ چارہ کھلایا تو ان میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔
اوپر جو آیا کہ سائمہ جانور میں زکوۃ ہے تو اب سائمہ جانور کی تشریح فرماتے ہیں۔ سائمہ جانور یعنی چرنے والے جانور اس کو کہیں گے جو سال کے آدھے یا آدھے سے زیادہ مہینوں میں گھاس چر کر زندگی گزارتا ہو۔ لیکن اگر سال کے آدھے یا آدھے سے زیادہ مہینوں میں گھر کا چارہ کھا کر زندگی گزارتے ہوں تو اس کو علوفہ کہتے ہیں۔ اور علوفہ میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ اور یہ دلیل بھی ہے حدثني ثمامة ابن عبد الله بن انس ان انسا حدثه ... فاذا كانت سائمة الرجل ناقصة من اربعين شاة واحدة فليس فيها صدقة (بخاری شریف ، باب زکوة الغنم ص ۱۹۵، نمبر ۱۴۵۴ ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۱۵۷۰) اس حدیث میں سائمہ کا لفظ ہے اس لئے سائمہ میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ انت الرعی : گھاس چرنا۔ علف : گھر کا چارہ کھانا۔
(12) And sa'imah is that which suffices with grazing for most of the year; if it is fed for half the year or more, then no zakat is due on it. (12) Sa'imah, grazing animals, are those that suffice with grazing for most of the year. So if the animal is fed fodder for half a year or more, then there is no zakat on them. It has come earlier that there is zakat on sa'imah animals, so now they explain the definition of sa'imah. Sa'imah animals, i.e., grazing animals, are those that spend half or more than half the months of the year grazing on grass. But if they spend half or more than half the months eating home fodder, then it is called 'ulufah (fodder-fed). And there is no zakat on 'ulufah. The proof has already passed. And this is also a proof: Thumamah ibn Abdullah ibn Anas narrated that Anas said: '... if a man's sa'imah is less than forty sheep by one, then there is no sadaqah on it.' (Bukhari, chapter on zakat of sheep, p.195 no.1454; Abu Dawud no.1570). In this hadith, the word sa'imah is used, therefore zakat is wajib on sa'imah. Ar-ra'y: grazing on grass. 'Aluf: eating home fodder.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage defines sa'imah (grazing livestock) and clarifies the condition for zakat. The matn states that sa'imah is livestock that depends on grazing for most of the year. If they are fed fodder for half the year or more, they are not sa'imah and no zakat is due. The commentary explains that animals fed at home are called 'ulufah and are exempt from zakat. A hadith is cited that mentions sa'imah, indicating that the ruling applies specifically to grazing animals. The key distinction is the majority of the year: grazing vs. fodder-fed.

Key Terms
سائمة (sa'imah): Livestock that graze on natural pasture for most of the year.
علوفة ('ulufah): Livestock fed on fodder at home for most of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because they are livestock
B) No, because they are not sa'imah (grazing for most of the year)
C) Yes, but only for the months they grazed
D) Only if the owner chooses to pay

Key Takeaway
Only livestock that graze for the majority of the year (sa'imah) are subject to zakat; animals fed at home for half or more are exempt.

Zakat on Excess (Afwu): Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of afwu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on zakat of excess (afwu) and explain the practical difference using the example of 203 dirhams.

Core Idea
Zakat is wajib only on the nisab, not on excess below a new nisab according to the relied-upon view.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known dispute about whether zakat is due on the excess amount (afwu) beyond the nisab. This lesson presents the positions of the founding imams, illustrates the practical impact with a concrete example, and examines the hadith evidence that solidifies the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
Recognize that the core question is: does zakat become wajib on the amount exceeding the nisab (e.g., 3 dirhams above 200)?
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: zakat only on the nisab (afwu exempt). Muhammad and Zufar: zakat on both nisab and afwu proportionally.
3
Work through the example
Apply the dispute to a person with 203 dirhams for a year. Calculate zakat under each view, then see the effect if the 3 extra dirhams are lost before payment.
Under the first view, zakat remains 5 dirhams; under the second, it reduces by 0.25 dirhams.
4
Examine the dalil
The hadith of Mu'adh explicitly prohibits taking zakat from the fraction until it reaches 40 dirhams. This text takes precedence over qiyas.
The hadith is a Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is stronger due to direct textual evidence and is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۶) (۱۳) زکوۃ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نصاب میں ہے عضو نہیں ہے اور امام محمد اور زفر نے فرمایا دونوں میں واجب ہے۔
مثلا دو سو درہم پر زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے اور کسی کے پاس دو سو میں درہم ہیں تو امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کی رائے یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ دوسو در ہم ہی پر پانچ درہم واجب ہوئی ، باقی تمیں درہم عضو ہے زیادہ ہے اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی وہ معاف ہے۔ چنانچہ سال گزرنے کے بعد تمہیں درہم ہلاک ہو جائے تو دو سو درہم پر جو پانچ درہم زکوۃ واجب ہوئی تھی اس میں کچھ کم نہیں ہوگی پانچ درہم ہی دینا ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد اور امام زفر کے نزدیک عضو پر بھی زکوۃ واجب ہے تو گویا کہ دو سو تمیں درہم پر پانچ درہم واجب ہوئی اس لئے تھیں درہم ہلاک ہو گئے تو اس حساب سے پانچ درہم زکوۃ میں پینسٹھ (۲۵) پیسے کی کمی آئے گی۔ اور چار درہم پینتیس (۳۵) پیسے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ امام شیخین کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن معاذ ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم امره حين وجهه الى اليمن ان لاتأخذ من الكسر شيئا اذا كانت الورق مائتى درهم فخذ منها خمسة دراهم ولا تأخذ مما زاد شيئا حتى تبلغ اربعين درهما واذا بلغ
صلى الله
(ج) آپ نے فرمایا کسی نے مال کا استفادہ کیا تو اس پر زکوۃ نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ اس پر سال گزر جائے۔
(13) Zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is on the nisab, not on the afwu (excess). And Imam Muhammad and Zufar said: it is wajib on both. For example: zakat is wajib on two hundred dirhams, and someone has two hundred and three dirhams. So Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's opinion is that zakat is wajib on just the two hundred dirhams: five dirhams. The remaining three dirhams are afwu, excess, no zakat is wajib on it; it is forgiven. So if after the year passes those three dirhams are destroyed, the five dirhams that were wajib on the two hundred are not reduced; he must give five dirhams. And according to Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar, zakat is wajib on the afwu as well. So if he had two hundred and three, then five dirhams were wajib; if the three dirhams are destroyed, then according to this calculation, the five dirhams zakat will be reduced by twenty-five (25) paise, and he must give four dirhams and thirty-five (35) paise. The evidence of the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is the hadith: from Mu'adh that the Messenger of Allah, when he sent him to Yemen, ordered him not to take anything from the fraction (kisr). When the silver reaches two hundred dirhams, take five dirhams from it, and do not take anything from what exceeds until it reaches forty dirhams. And when it reaches... (The hadith continues but is cut off in OCR.)
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether zakat is due on the excess (afwu) above the nisab. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that zakat is only on the exact nisab amount; any extra (like three dirhams above 200) is exempt until it itself becomes a nisab (i.e., 40 dirhams). Muhammad and Zufar say zakat is due on the excess proportionally. The example illustrates the practical difference: if 3 dirhams above 200 are destroyed, the first view sees no change (still 5 dirhams due), while the second view calculates a reduction. The proof from a hadith of Mu'adh supports Abu Hanifa's position: 'do not take anything from the fraction until it reaches forty.' This is a key example of how the Hanafi masters can differ within the school.

Key Terms
عضو (afwu): The excess amount above the nisab that is not yet a full nisab itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if someone has 230 dirhams, on how much is zakat wajib?
A) On all 230 dirhams
B) On 200 dirhams only
C) On 230 dirhams minus 40 (which is 190)
D) On 40 dirhams only

Key Takeaway
Zakat on excess (afwu) is not wajib until it reaches a full nisab; this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Definition and Ruling of Sa'imah (Grazing Animals)
Defines sa'imah and states ruling on zakat for non-sa'imah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sa'imah, state the ruling for non-sa'imah ('ulufa), and cite the hadith evidence for the condition of grazing.

Core Idea
Zakat is wajib on sa'imah; animals fed fodder for half the year or more incur no zakat.

This passage from a Hanafi text clarifies a key condition for zakat on livestock. Many assume zakat is due on any owned cattle, but the school distinguishes between animals that depend on natural grazing (sa'imah) and those fed at home ('ulufa). Understanding this distinction is essential to correctly applying zakat obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of sa'imah
Read the passage and determine what makes an animal sa'imah according to the Hanafi school. Look for the key phrase 'taktafi bi al-ra'y fi akthar al-hawl'.
The ruling rests on the majority of the year — not a specific number of months, but more than half.
2
Identify the ruling for non-sa'imah ( 'ulufa )
Find the condition that nullifies the status of sa'imah. Note the phrase 'fa-in 'alafaha nisf al-hawl aw akthar fala zakata fiha'.
The threshold is half the year or more of fodder feeding.
3
Locate the dalil (hadith evidence)
The author cites a hadith to support the ruling. Identify the source (Bukhari, Abu Dawood) and the key word from the hadith (sa'imah) that proves the condition.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah (how the dalil proves the ruling)
Understand why the hadith is used: the Prophet ﷺ mentioned 'sa'imah' in the condition for zakat, implying that non-sa'imah are exempt.

Source Text

[485] (12) والسائمة هى التى تكتفى بالرعى فى اكثر الحول فان علفها نصف الحول او اكثر فلا زكوة فيها
[485] (12) سائمہ، چرنے والے جانوران کو کہتے ہیں کہ وہ سال کے اکثر حصہ میں چرنے پر اکتفا کرے، پس اگر جانور کو آدھا سال یا زیادہ چارہ کھلایا تو ان میں زکوۃ نہیں ہے۔ اوپر جو آیا کہ سائمہ جانور میں زکوۃ ہے تو اب سائمہ جانور کی تشریح فرماتے ہیں۔ سائمہ جانور یعنی چرنے والے جانور اس کو کہیں گے جو سال کے آدھے یا آدھے سے زیادہ مہینوں میں گھاس چر کر زندگی گزارتا ہو۔ لیکن اگر سال کے آدھے یا آدھے سے زیادہ مہینوں میں گھر کا چارہ کھا کر زندگی گزارتے ہوں تو اس کو علوفہ کہتے ہیں۔ اور علوفہ میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ اور یہ دلیل بھی ہے حدثني ثمامة ابن عبد الله بن انس ان انسا حدثه ... فاذا كانت سائمة الرجل ناقصة من اربعين شاة واحدة فليس فيها صدقة (بخاری شریف ، باب زکوة الغنم ص ۱۹۵، نمبر ۱۴۵۴ ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۱۵۷۰) اس حدیث میں سائمہ کا لفظ ہے اس لئے سائمہ میں زکوۃ واجب ہوگی ۔ انت الرعی : گھاس چرنا۔ علف : گھر کا چارہ کھانا۔
[485] (12) And the grazing animals are those that suffice with grazing for most of the year. So if one feeds them fodder for half the year or more, then there is no zakat on them. [485] (12) Sa'imah, meaning grazing animals, are those that suffice with grazing for the majority of the year. So if the animal is fed fodder for half a year or more, then there is no zakat on them. Above it came that zakat is obligatory on grazing animals, so now they explain the definition of grazing animals. Sa'imah animals, meaning grazing animals, are called those that live by grazing grass for half or more than half of the months of the year. But if they live by eating home fodder for half or more than half of the months of the year, then it is called 'ulufa, and there is no zakat obligatory on 'ulufa. The proof has passed before. And this is also a proof: Thumama ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Anas narrated from Anas... 'When the grazing animals of a man are short by one sheep from forty, then there is no sadaqah on them' (Bukhari, Bab Zakat al-Ghanam, p.195, no.1454; Abu Dawood, no.1570). In this hadith, the word sa'imah is used, therefore zakat will be obligatory on sa'imah. al-Ra'i: grazing grass. 'Alf: eating home fodder.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of sa'imah (grazing animals) and its ruling. The author first quotes the matn: Sa'imah are animals that depend on grazing for most of the year. If they are fed fodder (alf) for half the year or more, they are not considered sa'imah and no zakat is due. The commentary explains that if the animal grazes for half or more than half of the year, it is sa'imah; if it eats home fodder for half or more, it is called 'ulufa and no zakat is due. The proof is a hadith from Bukhari and Abu Dawood where the Prophet (peace be upon him) used the word sa'imah, indicating that zakat is only on grazing animals. The author also distinguishes between ra'y (grazing) and 'alf (fodder). This is a standard Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
سائمة (sā'imah): Animals that depend on grazing (ra'y) for most of the year, i.e., at least half the year.
علف (‘alf): Feeding animals fodder at home.
رعي (ra‘y): Grazing on natural pasture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It must graze for the entire year.
B) It must be fed fodder for most of the year.
C) It must depend on grazing for most (akthar) of the year.
D) It must never be fed any fodder.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of zakat on livestock is conditional upon the animals being sa'imah, which in Hanafi law means they graze for most of the year; if fed fodder for half the year or more, no zakat is due.

Zakat on Mustafad: Shafi'i Evidence and Hanafi Response
Presents Shafi'i view that zakat on mustafad requires hawlaan al-hawl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Shafi'i position on zakat on mustafad, identify their dalil, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
A hadith requiring a full year for mustafad is read differently: Hanafis add it to existing wealth, Shafi'is require a separate hawl.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute over zakat on newly acquired wealth. Imam al-Shafi'i relies on a specific hadith to argue that each new acquisition must complete its own year before zakat is due. The Hanafi school, however, integrates mustafad into the existing zakat year. Understanding this difference is crucial for accurate zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine the exact point of disagreement: whether newly acquired wealth (mustafad) requires its own separate year (hawl) for zakat to become due, or whether it can be added to the existing zakatable wealth and zakat paid at the end of the original year.
The core issue is the condition of hawlaan al-hawl for mustafad.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that zakat on mustafad is not obligatory until a full lunar year passes from the date of acquisition, regardless of the owner's existing zakat year.
This position is based on a specific hadith.
3
Examine the Shafi'i dalil
The hadith from Ibn 'Umar is cited: 'Whoever acquires wealth, there is no zakat on him until a year passes over it.' Identify the chain (ahad) and the apparent meaning (zanni al-dalala).
The hadith directly supports a separate hawl requirement.
4
Note the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (implied), zakat is on the nisab as a whole. Mustafad is added to the existing wealth, and zakat is due on the total at the end of the original hawl, without requiring a separate hawl for the new wealth.
The Hanafi view is not fully elaborated here but contrasts with the Shafi'i view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical difference: If a person acquires wealth mid-year, Hanafis include it in the current year's zakat, while Shafi'is defer zakat on it until a full year from acquisition passes.
This affects both the timing and the amount of zakat due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والزكوة عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف في النصاب انده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جب تک مال مستفاد پر سال نہ گزر جائے زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمر قال قال رسول الله الا الله من استفاد مالا فلا زكوة عليه حتى يحول عليه الحول (الف) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء لا زکوۃ على المال المستفاد حتی حال علیہ الحول ص ۱۳۷ نمبر ۶۳۱ دار قطنی ، باب وجوب الزكوة بالحول ج ثانی ص سے لے نمبر۱۸۷۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جب تک خود مال مستفاد پر سال نہ گزر جائے اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
And zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is on the nisab? And Imam Shafi'i says: Zakat is not obligatory on newly acquired wealth until a year passes over it. Their proof is this hadith: from Ibn 'Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, whoever acquires wealth, there is no zakat on him until a year passes over it.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a la zakata 'ala al-mal al-mustafad hatta yahula 'alayhi al-hawl, p.137 no.631; Dar Qutni, Bab wujub al-zakah bi al-hawl, vol.2 p.?? no.1877). From this hadith, it is understood that zakat is not obligatory on the mustafad itself until a year passes over it.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute. The author states that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, zakat is on the nisab (the principal amount), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that zakat on newly acquired wealth (mustafad) is not obligatory until a full year (hawl) passes from the time of acquisition. The proof for al-Shafi'i is the hadith from Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet said there is no zakat on mustafad until a year passes. The author then comments that from this hadith, it is understood that mustafad itself requires its own hawl. Note: The Hanafi position on mustafad is not fully detailed here, but the context suggests that Hanafis treat mustafad differently, perhaps by adding it to existing wealth and zakat on the whole after the hawl of the original wealth. This passage is a concise statement of the Shafi'i proof.

Key Terms
مستفاد (mustafād): Newly acquired wealth, e.g., inheritance, gift, or earnings, acquired during the current zakat year.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The dispute over mustafad hinges on whether the hadith requiring a full year is applied strictly or overridden by istihsan, leading to different zakat schedules.

Zakat on Surplus: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Afw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat on surplus above nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on zakat on surplus ('afw) and identify which hadith proofs each side uses.

Core Idea
Zakat on surplus: Abu Hanifa exempts it; Muhammad and Zufar require proportional payment.

The zakat obligation on cash wealth is straightforward for the exact nisab (200 dirhams), but what about surplus wealth that falls short of the next threshold? Within the Hanafi school, a well-known dispute exists between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and two other leading imams (Muhammad and Zufar) on this very point. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: zakat is due only on the nisab (e.g., 200 dirhams). Any surplus ('afw) up to the next complete nisab (40 dirhams) is exempt.
This is the position that later Hanafi authorities often adopt as mufta bihi.
2
Identify the opposing view within the school
Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar hold that zakat is obligatory on both the nisab and the surplus, calculated proportionally.
They consider the surplus a blessing deserving of zakat.
3
Examine the proof of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Analyze the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet commands not to take from the fraction (kusr) until it reaches a complete forty dirhams. How does this support exemption?
The key phrase is 'لا تأخذ من الكسر شيئا' – do not take anything from the fraction.
4
Analyze the proof of Muhammad and Zufar
Consider the hadith 'فإذا كانت مائتي درهم ففيها خمسة دراهم فما زاد فعلى حساب ذلك' – whatever exceeds, calculate accordingly. How does this support proportional zakat?
This hadith appears to imply that any increase is also subject to the same rate.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the surplus is destroyed after a year, how does the zakat obligation change under each view? Apply the scenario: 230 dirhams, 30 dirhams lost.
Majority: zakat remains 5 dirhams. Opposing view: zakat reduces to 4.35 dirhams (approximately).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[486) (13) زکوۃ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک نصاب میں ہے عضو نہیں ہے اور امام محمد اور زفر نے فرمایا دونوں میں واجب ہے۔ مثلا دو سو درہم پر زکوۃ واجب ہوتی ہے اور کسی کے پاس دو سو میں درہم ہیں تو امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کی رائے یہ ہے کہ زکوۃ دوسو در ہم ہی پر پانچ درہم واجب ہوئی ، باقی تمیں درہم عضو ہے زیادہ ہے اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی وہ معاف ہے۔ چنانچہ سال گزرنے کے بعد تمیں درہم ہلاک ہو جائے تو دو سو درہم پر جو پانچ درہم زکوۃ واجب ہوئی تھی اس میں کچھ کم نہیں ہوگی پانچ درہم ہی دینا ہوگی ۔ اور امام محمد اور امام زفر کے نزدیک عضو پر بھی زکوۃ واجب ہے تو گویا کہ دو سو تمیں درہم پر پانچ درہم واجب ہوئی اس لئے تھیں درہم ہلاک ہو گئے تو اس حساب سے پانچ درہم زکوۃ میں پینسٹھ (۲۵) پیسے کی کمی آئے گی۔ اور چار درہم پینتیس (۳۵) پیسے زکوۃ واجب ہوگی۔ امام شیخین کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن معاذ ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم امره حين وجهه الى اليمن ان لاتأخذ من الكسر شيئا اذا كانت الورق مائتى درهم فخذ منها خمسة دراهم ولا تأخذ مما زاد شيئا حتى تبلغ اربعين درهما واذا بلغ اربعین درهما فخذ منه درهما (الف) (دار قطنی ۳ باب لیس فی الکسرشی میں ۸۰ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ دوسو درہم کے بعد جب تک چالیس درہم نہ ہو جائے تو زکوۃ میں کچھ کمی نہیں ہوگی۔ فائدہ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصل نصاب اور عفو دونوں اللہ کی نعمت ہیں اس لئے زکوۃ دونوں پر لازم ہوئی۔ اس لئے جب عفو ہلاک ہوا تو زکوۃ کا کچھ حصہ اس کے حساب سے ساقط ہوا۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ فاذا كانت مائتى دراهم ففيها خمسة دراهم فمازاد فعلى حساب ذلک (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی زکوة السائمة نمبر ۱۵۷۲ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۵ فی الزيادة في الفریضہ ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۳۶۴، نمبر ۹۹۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو زیادہ ہوز کوۃ میں اس کا بھی حساب ہوگا۔
عاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جب حضرت معاذ کو یمن کی طرف متوجہ کیا تو آپ نے ان کو حکم دیا کہ کسر میں کچھ نہ لے۔ جب چاندی دو سو درہم ہو جائے تو اس میں پانچ در ہم لو۔ اور جو زیادہ ہو جائے اس میں کچھ نہ لو۔ یہاں تک کہ چالیس درہم کو پہنچ جائے۔ اور جب چالیس درہم پہنچ جائے تو اس سے ایک درہم لو (ب ) حضرت عطا سے منقول ہے کہ کوئی آدمی اپنے مال کی زکوۃ نکالے پھر زکوۃ ضائع ہو جائے تو اس سے کافی ہو جائے گی۔
[486] (13) Zakat according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf is on the nisab, not on the 'udw (surplus). And Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar said: it is obligatory on both. For example, zakat is obligatory on two hundred dirhams. If someone has two hundred and thirty dirhams, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, only five dirhams are obligatory on the two hundred dirhams, the remaining thirty dirhams are 'udw (surplus) and are exempt, no zakat is due on them. Thus, if after the year passes the thirty dirhams are destroyed, the five dirhams zakat due on the two hundred dirhams remains unchanged; five dirhams must still be paid. According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar, zakat is obligatory on the surplus as well. So on two hundred and thirty dirhams, five dirhams would be due proportionally. If the thirty dirhams are destroyed, then the zakat reduces proportionally: twenty-five cents less, and four dirhams and thirty-five cents would be due. The proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is this hadith: from Mu'adh that the Messenger of Allah, when he sent him to Yemen, commanded him to take nothing from the fraction (kusr). When the silver reaches two hundred dirhams, take from it five dirhams, and do not take anything from what exceeds until it reaches forty dirhams. When it reaches forty dirhams, take from it one dirham. (Dar Qutni, Bab laysa fi al-kusr shay', no.1886). From this hadith it is understood that after two hundred dirhams, until forty dirhams are accumulated, there is no change in zakat. Benefit: Imam Muhammad's proof is that both the original nisab and the 'afw are blessings of Allah, so zakat is obligatory on both. Therefore, when the 'afw is destroyed, a portion of the zakat drops proportionally. In a hadith: 'When there are two hundred dirhams, in them five dirhams, and whatever exceeds, then according to that calculation.' (Abu Dawood, Bab fi zakati al-sa'imah, no.1572; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 5 fi al-ziyada fi al-faridah, vol.2, p.1364, no.9947). From this hadith it is understood that whatever exceeds also has its calculation in zakat. Footnote: (a) When the Prophet sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he commanded him not to take anything from the fraction. When silver reaches two hundred dirhams, take five dirhams, and do not take anything from what exceeds until it reaches forty dirhams. When it reaches forty dirhams, take from it one dirham. (b) It is narrated from 'Ata that if a man takes out the zakat of his wealth and it is lost, it suffices for him.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether zakat is due on the nisab only or also on the surplus ('udw/afw) above the nisab. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that zakat is only on the exact nisab amount, and any surplus up to the next threshold (e.g., 40 dirhams) is exempt ('afw). Their proof is the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet instructed not to take from the fraction (kusr) until it reaches a complete nisab. Muhammad and Zufar argue that zakat is proportional on all wealth, citing the hadith 'whatever exceeds, calculate accordingly'. The commentator explains the practical difference: if surplus is destroyed, the zakat due does not change in the first view but reduces proportionally in the second. The footnote further explains that the hadith of Mu'adh exempts surplus, while the other hadith supports proportional calculation. This is a classic ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
عفو (‘afw): The surplus wealth above the nisab that does not reach the next complete nisab threshold.
كسر (kusr): Fractional amount, i.e., surplus less than a complete nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith of Mu'adh cited by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the threshold at which zakat becomes due on the surplus?
A) When the surplus reaches 10 dirhams.
B) When the surplus reaches 40 dirhams.
C) When the total wealth reaches 240 dirhams.
D) There is no threshold; surplus is always exempt.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the ruling on zakat on surplus depends on which hadith proof is given priority; the majority exempts surplus until the next complete nisab.

Zakat Obligation Drops if Wealth Is Destroyed: A Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute
States that zakat is dropped if wealth is destroyed after obligation, with Shafi'i opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat when wealth is destroyed unintentionally, explain the qiyas used, and identify the practical consequence of the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
If the wealth subject to zakat perishes, the obligation drops—the subject is gone.

Zakat becomes wajib after the completion of a lunar year (hawl) on nisab-level wealth. But what if the wealth is destroyed before the owner pays? This lesson examines the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether the obligation remains. The Hanafi school holds that unintentional destruction cancels the obligation, while the Shafi'i school maintains it remains binding. We will explore the proofs and the practical consequences of this dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the rule: if wealth is destroyed unintentionally after zakat becomes wajib, the obligation drops (saqat). If destroyed intentionally, it remains.
The act is zakat payment; the ruling is that it is no longer required.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The source uses a qiyas: like a slave who commits a crime then dies, the master's liability (daman) drops. Also, an athar from 'Ata states that if zakat is taken out and lost, it suffices, implying a fortiori that if the wealth itself is destroyed, the obligation drops.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position and proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that zakat remains wajib even after destruction, analogizing to sadaqat al-fitr. He also cites an athar from Mughira that one must pay again if zakat is lost after being taken out.
The Shafi'i proof relies on the idea that obligation is not contingent on the continued existence of the wealth.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response favors the athar of 'Ata and argues that the case of wealth destruction is stronger than loss after segregation, so the obligation drops.
This is a matter of tarjih (preference) among conflicting evidences.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If wealth is destroyed after the hawl, Hanafis say no zakat is due; Shafi'is require payment from other assets.
This affects the mufti's answer in real cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[487] (14) واذا هلك المال بعد وجوب الزكوة سقطت
[487] (14) زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے بعد اگر مال ہلاک ہو جائے تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
نصاب پر سال گزر گیا جس کی وجہ سے زکوۃ واجب ہوئی اور ادا کرنے کی بھی قدرت ہوئی لیکن آجکل کرتا رہا اور اس درمیان مال بلاک ہو گیا تو حنفیہ کے نشد یک زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر جان کر مال کو ہلاک کر دیا تو زکوۃ واجب رہے گی۔ زکوۃ کا مل مال تھا اور اب محل ہی باقی نہیں رہا تو زکوۃ کس پر لازم کریں۔ جیسے جنایت کرنے والا غلام مر جائے تو مولی اب کس کو سپرد کرے گا۔ مولی سے ضمان ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح مال کی ہلاکت کے بعد زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر آدھا مال ہلاک ہوا تو آدھی زکوة ساقط ہوگی۔ اس کی ایک مثال یہ قول بھی ہے عن عطا فی الرجل اذا اخرج زكوة ماله فضاعت انها تجزى عنه (ب) (مصنف ابن الي هيبة ، ۸۹ ما قالوانی الرجل اخرج زکوۃ مالہ فضاعت ج ثانی ہیں (۴۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ کا مال نکال چکا ہو پھر ضائع ہو گیا ہو تو وہ کافی ہوگا تو پورا مال ہی ہلاک ہو گیا ہو تو بدرجہ اولی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ انده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ زکوۃ واجب ہو چکی تھی اس لئے مال ہلاک ہونے کے بعد بھی واجب ہی رہے گی۔ جس طرح صدقۂ فطر ہو واجب ہونے کے بعد مال ہلاک ہو جائے پھر بھی صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہی رہتا ہے۔
عن مغير ة عن اصحابه قالوا: اذا اخرج زكوة ماله فضاعت فليزك مرة اخرى (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، ۸۹ ما قالوافی الرجل اخرج زکوۃ ماله فضاعت ، ج ثانی ، ص ۴۰۸ نمبر ۱۰۴۸۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوبارہ ادا کرے۔
[487] (14) And if the wealth is destroyed after the obligation of zakat, it (the obligation) drops. [487] (14) If wealth is destroyed after zakat becomes wajib, then zakat drops. The nisab completed a year, so zakat became wajib, and there was ability to pay, but he delayed, and in the meantime the wealth was destroyed. According to the Hanafis, the zakat drops. And if he intentionally destroyed the wealth, then zakat remains wajib. The wealth was the subject of zakat, and now the subject no longer exists, so what would zakat be imposed on? Like if a slave who committed a crime dies, then to whom will the master surrender? The liability (daman) drops from the master. Similarly, after the destruction of wealth, zakat drops. And if half the wealth is destroyed, then half the zakat drops. An example of this is the saying of 'Ata: 'If a man takes out the zakat of his wealth and it is lost, it suffices for him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 89 ma qalu fi al-rajul akhraja zakata malihi fada'at, vol.2, p.408). From this athar, it is understood that if he had already taken out the zakat and it was lost, it is sufficient; then if the entire wealth is destroyed, it is even more so that zakat drops. And Imam al-Shafi'i says: Zakat had become wajib, so even after the wealth is destroyed, it remains wajib, just as sadaqat al-fitr, after it becomes wajib, if the wealth is destroyed, sadaqat al-fitr remains wajib. From Mughira from his companions: 'If a man takes out the zakat of his wealth and it is lost, let him pay zakat again.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, same reference, no.10488). From this athar, it is understood that he should pay again.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when wealth is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory but before payment. The Hanafi position is that the obligation drops because the subject (wealth) no longer exists. If the destruction is intentional, however, the obligation remains. The author analogizes to a slave who dies after committing a crime; the master's liability drops. The proof is an athar from 'Ata that if zakat is taken out and lost, it is sufficient, implying that if the wealth itself is destroyed, the obligation drops. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the obligation remains, like sadaqat al-fitr, which is not dropped by destruction of wealth after obligation. Another athar from Mughira suggests that if zakat is lost after being taken out, one should pay again, which seems contradictory but is used by Shafi'i. The Hanafi response is that the athar of 'Ata is more specific. This is an inter-madhhab dispute with practical implications.

Key Terms
ساقط (sāqiṭ): Dropped, cancelled; the obligation of zakat is no longer binding.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability, guarantee; here, the liability of the master for the slave's crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person's wealth is destroyed by fire after the zakat year completes but before he pays, what is the ruling?
A) He must still pay zakat from other wealth.
B) The zakat obligation drops.
C) He must pay zakat only if the destruction was intentional.
D) He must pay zakat because it is a debt owed to Allah.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, unintentional destruction of zakatable wealth after the year drops the obligation.

Permissibility of Paying Zakat Before the Year Completes
States that it is permissible to pay zakat before the hawl if one owns nisab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying zakat before the hawl and identify the condition for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Paying zakat early is valid if you already own nisab.

This lesson addresses a common question: can zakat be paid before the zakat year ends? The Hanafi school provides a clear permission, provided a key condition is met. Let's examine the ruling and its condition directly from the classical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is giving zakat before the lunar year (hawl) completes. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible).
This is a relaxation (rukhsah), not an obligation.
2
Locate the condition
The passage states the condition explicitly: the person must be owner of a full nisab at the time of early payment.
If nisab is not owned at payment, the early payment may not count as zakat.

Source Text

[488] (15) And if he gives zakat before the year (completes) while he is owner of the nisab, it is permissible. [488] (15) If he gives zakat before the completion of the year, and the situation is that he is owner of the nisab, it is permissible.

Commentary
This passage contains a concise ruling: It is permissible (ja'iz) to pay zakat before the completion of the zakat year (hawl), provided that the person is already the owner of a full nisab. This is a relaxation (rukhsah) allowed by the Hanafi school. The ruling does not require any proof in this passage; it is simply stated as a legal permission. The commentary adds no further detail, implying this is a well-established ruling.

Key Terms

Zakat on the 'Afw (Surplus) – Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat on the 'afw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on zakat on the 'afw (surplus) and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement of Muhammad and Zufar, including their proofs.

Core Idea
The surplus ('afw) between nisab thresholds is exempt from zakat per Abu Hanifa; Muhammad and Zufar obligate zakat on it proportionally.

This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute about a seemingly small but practically significant detail: does zakat apply to the surplus wealth that sits between the standard nisab thresholds? Imam Abu Hanifa held that such surplus ('afw) is exempt until it itself reaches the next full nisab (e.g., 40 dirhams for silver). His two students, Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar, disagreed, arguing that both the principal and the surplus are blessings from Allah and thus both should be subject to zakat proportionally. By examining their proofs, you will deepen your understanding of how Hanafi jurisprudence handles fractional increases in wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the dispute is about the 'afw – the surplus wealth above a nisab that has not yet reached the next full nisab threshold (e.g., between 200 and 240 dirhams).
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa: no zakat on the 'afw. Only full nisab increments trigger zakat.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State the opposing view
Imam Muhammad and Zufar: zakat is wajib on both the principal and the surplus proportionally.
They base this on the hadith of forty dirhams and a rational argument.
4
Analyse the proofs
Examine the two hadiths cited: the Daraqutni hadith (used by Muhammad) and the Abu Dawud hadith (used by Abu Hanifa). Also note the rational argument that both are Allah's blessings.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the dispute to a concrete example: a person with 230 dirhams. Under Abu Hanifa, zakat is due on 200 dirhams only; under Muhammad, on all 230 proportionally.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دون العفو وقال محمد وزفر تجب فيهما اربعین درهما فخذ منه درهما (الف) (دار قطنی ۳ باب لیس فی الکسرشی میں ۸۰ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے پتہ چلا کہ دوسو درہم کے بعد جب تک چالیس درہم نہ ہو جائے تو زکوۃ میں کچھ کمی نہیں ہوگی۔ فائدہ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصل نصاب اور عفو دونوں اللہ کی نعمت ہیں اس لئے زکوۃ دونوں پر لازم ہوئی۔ اس لئے جب عفو ہلاک ہوا تو زکوۃ کا کچھ حصہ اس کے حساب سے ساقط ہوا۔

حدیث میں ہے۔ فاذا كانت مائتى دراهم ففيها خمسة دراهم فمازاد فعلى حساب ذلک (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی زکوة السائمة نمبر ۱۵۷۲ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۵ فی الزيادة في الفريضہ ، ج ثانی ، ص ۱۳۶۴، نمبر ۹۹۴۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو زیادہ ہوز کوۃ میں اس کا بھی حساب ہوگا۔
Except for the surplus, and Muhammad and Zufar said zakat is obligatory on both. 'When it reaches forty dirhams, take from it one dirham.' (Al-Daraqutni, Chapter: There is no [zakat] on the break, no. 1886) From this hadith it is known that after two hundred dirhams, until forty dirhams are not reached, there is no reduction in zakat. Benefit: Imam Muhammad's proof is that the original nisab and the surplus are both blessings of Allah, therefore zakat became obligatory on both. Therefore, when the surplus perished, some portion of zakat was dropped according to its calculation.

In a hadith: 'When there are two hundred dirhams, then in them are five dirhams; and what exceeds, then according to that calculation.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Zakat of Grazing Animals, no. 1572; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, on the increase in the fard, vol. 2, p. 1364, no. 9947) From this hadith it is known that whatever increases, its zakat will also be calculated.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of zakat on the surplus ('afw) amount that lies between the nisab thresholds. The matn states the majority Hanafi position: no zakat on the 'afw. But Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar hold that zakat is obligatory on both the principal nisab and the surplus. The text first cites a hadith attributed to al-Daraqutni instructing to take one dirham when silver reaches forty dirhams—this is part of a longer hadith about zakat on silver in fractions. Then it explains Imam Muhammad's rational argument: both the original nisab and the surplus are divine provisions, so zakat should apply to both; thus, if the surplus perishes, a portion of the total zakat is waived proportionally. Another hadith from Abu Dawud supports the principle that zakat is calculated proportionally on any increase. The dispute is practical: if someone has 240 dirhams (200 nisab + 40 surplus), Abu Hanifa would exempt the 40, while Muhammad would require zakat on the entire 240 at 2.5%.

Key Terms
العفو (al-'afw): The surplus amount of wealth above the nisab that has not yet reached the next full nisab threshold (e.g., between 200 and 240 dirhams for silver).
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation, e.g., 200 dirhams for silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Zakat is not obligatory on the 'afw
B) Zakat is obligatory on both the original nisab and the 'afw
C) Zakat is only obligatory on the 'afw
D) Zakat is waived if the 'afw perishes

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the 'afw (surplus between nisab thresholds) is exempt from zakat according to the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa, but an intra-school disagreement exists.

Zakat Obligation Drops if Wealth Perishes Unintentionally
Ruling that zakat obligation drops if wealth is destroyed after it becomes due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat when wealth perishes after the obligation becomes due and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Zakat is a right on wealth itself; if the wealth perishes unintentionally, the obligation drops.

Many students assume that once zakat becomes obligatory, it becomes an absolute personal debt that cannot be waived. However, the Hanafi school takes a nuanced view: zakat is a right attached to the wealth itself. This lesson explores the ruling and its proof, along with the Shafi'i counter-argument, so you can confidently handle a common real-world scenario.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The act is the obligation to pay zakat on wealth after a lunar year has passed. The Hanafi ruling: if the wealth perishes unintentionally (e.g., natural disaster), the obligation drops (saqit).
Note that this applies only to unintentional destruction; intentional destruction does not drop the obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The text provides two proofs: an effect from 'Ata (a qawl sahabi) and a qiyas (analogy) with a slave who commits a crime and dies. Identify each proof and its source.
The effect from 'Ata is: 'If a man takes out the zakat of his wealth and it is lost, it suffices for him.' This implies a fortiori that if the entire wealth is lost, zakat is dropped.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the 'Ata effect, the wajh is: if already-separated zakat suffices when lost, then the original obligation is even more rightly dropped when the wealth itself perishes. For the qiyas: just as a master's liability drops when a criminal slave dies, so too the zakat obligation drops when the wealth (the subject) perishes.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) based on the extinction of the subject matter.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and evaluate
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that zakat becomes a debt on the owner, analogous to sadaqat al-fitr, and is not extinguished by loss of wealth. Evaluate the Hanafi response: the obligation is not a personal debt but a right in the wealth itself.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant: in Shafi'i school, you must pay from other wealth; in Hanafi, you owe nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۸۷] (۱۴) زکوۃ واجب ہونے کے بعد اگر مال ہلاک ہو جائے تو زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔

نصاب پر سال گزر گیا جس کی وجہ سے زکوۃ واجب ہوئی اور ادا کرنے کی بھی قدرت ہوئی لیکن آجکل کرتا رہا اور اس درمیان مال بلاک ہو گیا تو حنفیہ کے نشد یک زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر جان کر مال کو ہلاک کر دیا تو زکوۃ واجب رہے گی۔ زکوۃ کا مل مال تھا اور اب محل ہی باقی نہیں رہا تو زکوۃ کس پر لازم کریں۔ جیسے جنایت کرنے والا غلام مر جائے تو مولی اب کس کو سپرد کرے گا۔ مولی سے ضمان ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح مال کی ہلاکت کے بعد زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر آدھا مال ہلاک ہوا تو آدھی زکوة ساقط ہوگی۔ اس کی ایک مثال یہ قول بھی ہے عن عطا فی الرجل اذا اخرج زكوة ماله فضاعت انها تجزى عنه (ب) (مصنف ابن الي هيبة ، ۸۹ ما قالوانی الرجل اخرج زکوۃ مالہ فضاعت ج ثانی ہیں (۴۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ زکوۃ کا مال نکال چکا ہو پھر ضائع ہو گیا ہو تو وہ کافی ہوگا تو پورا مال ہی ہلاک ہو گیا ہو تو بدرجہ اولی زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ انده امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ زکوۃ واجب ہو چکی تھی اس لئے مال ہلاک ہونے کے بعد بھی واجب ہی رہے گی۔ جس طرح صدقۂ فطر ہو واجب ہونے کے بعد مال ہلاک ہو جائے پھر بھی صدقۃ الفطر واجب ہی رہتا ہے۔

عن مغير ة عن اصحابه قالوا: اذا اخرج زكوة ماله فضاعت فليزك مرة اخرى (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، ۸۹ ما قالوافی الرجل اخرج زکوۃ مالہ فضاعت ، ج ثانی ، ص ۴۰۸ نمبر ۱۰۴۸۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوبارہ ادا کرے۔
[487] (14) If wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, the zakat is dropped. The nisab had a complete year passed, so zakat became obligatory and he had the ability to pay, but he delayed and in the meantime the wealth was destroyed. According to the Hanafis, the zakat is dropped. But if he deliberately destroyed the wealth, zakat remains obligatory. The wealth was the subject of zakat, and now the subject no longer exists, so on what would zakat be liable? Like a slave who commits a crime and dies; the master will not hand over anything. The responsibility of the master is dropped. Similarly, after the destruction of wealth, zakat is dropped. And if half the wealth is destroyed, half the zakat is dropped. An example of this is the statement of 'Ata: 'If a man takes out the zakat of his wealth and it is lost, it suffices for him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 2, p. 408) From this effect it is known that if he had already taken out the zakat and it was lost, it is sufficient; so a fortiori if the entire wealth is destroyed, zakat is dropped. Then Imam Shafi'i says: Zakat had become obligatory, so even after the wealth is destroyed, it remains obligatory, just as sadaqat al-fitr, after becoming obligatory, if the wealth is destroyed, sadaqat al-fitr remains obligatory. From Mughirah, from his companions, they said: If he takes out the zakat of his wealth and it is lost, he should give zakat again. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) From this effect it is known that he should pay again.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the fate of zakat obligation when the wealth perishes after the obligation has become binding. The ruling: if the wealth is destroyed through no fault of the owner, the zakat obligation is dropped entirely (or proportionally if partially destroyed). This is because zakat is a right attached to the wealth itself; when the wealth ceases to exist, the right has no object. An analogy is given: if a slave who commits a crime dies, the master's liability to hand him over drops. However, if the owner deliberately destroys the wealth, the obligation remains, as it is a form of evasion. The text then contrasts the Shafi'i position, which holds that the obligation becomes a debt on the owner and is not extinguished by the loss of wealth, analogizing it to sadaqat al-fitr (which remains due even if one's wealth perishes after the obligation). The Hanafi position is supported by the precedent of 'Ata and a contrary effect from Mughirah's companions, but the Hanafis adopt the first view. The practical consequence: if someone's livestock die after the year has passed but before paying zakat, no zakat is due in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
هلاك المال (halak al-mal): The destruction or loss of the wealth that was subject to zakat.
ساقط (saqit): Dropped, fallen, no longer obligatory.
محل (mahall): The subject matter or locus of a legal right; here, the wealth on which zakat is due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if someone's zakatable wealth is destroyed through no fault of their own after the obligation has become due, what happens to the zakat?
A) It remains due and must be paid from other wealth
B) It is dropped and no longer obligatory
C) It must be paid only if the wealth is recovered
D) He must give zakat again next year

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat is a right attached to wealth; if the wealth perishes unintentionally, the obligation drops.

Permissibility of Advancing Zakat Before the Year
Ruling that zakat may be given before the completion of the lunar year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying zakat before the completion of the lunar year and identify the primary evidence from the Sunnah that supports it.

Core Idea
You may give zakat early once you own the nisab; the Prophet permitted al-Abbas to advance it.

This passage clarifies that the Hanafi school permits giving zakat before the lunar year concludes, provided one possesses the minimum nisab. The ruling is based on the explicit sunnah and the legal principle that the existence of the cause (nisab) suffices. You will examine the text and its proofs to understand this important practical concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? It is ta'jil al-zakah (advancing zakat). What is the hukm? The passage states it is 'ja'iz' (permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of al-Abbas, in which he asked the Prophet about advancing sadaqah and was permitted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The explicit permission (rukhsah) indicates that advancing is allowed.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The nisab is the cause (sabab) for zakat; since it is present, the payment is valid even before the year ends.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools require the year to pass absolutely, but the Hanafi position is adopted.

[۴۸۸] (۱۵) اگر سال مکمل ہونے سے پہلے زکوۃ دیدی اور حال یہ ہے کہ وہ نصاب کا مالک ہے تو جائز ہے۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل)
كتاب الزكوة
ری ایک آدمی نصاب کا مالک ہے لیکن اس نصاب پر سال نہیں گزرا ہے اور وہ ابھی زکوۃ ادا کر دینا چاہتا ہے تو جائز ہے۔ اکوۃ ادا ہو جائینگی۔
مال نصاب اصل سبب ہے اور وہ پایا گیا تو گویا کہ سبب پایا گیا اس لئے زکوۃ کی ادائیگی ہو جائیگی (۲) حدیث میں ہے عــن عـلـى ان العباس سأل النبي الله في تعجيل الصدقة قبل ان تحل فرخص له في ذلك (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی تجمیل الزکوة ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۶۲۴ ارترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی تجمیل الزکوۃ ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۶۷۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سال گزرنے سے پہلے زکوۃ ادا کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ حضرت عباس گو اس کی اجازت دی تھی۔

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عباس نے حضور سے زکوۃ جلدی دینے کے بارے میں پوچھا وقت آنے سے پہلے تو آپ نے اس بارے میں رخصت دیدی۔
[488] (15) If he gave zakat before the completion of the year, and he is the owner of the nisab, it is permissible.

Marginal note: (A) When the Prophet sent Mu'adh to Yemen, he commanded him not to take anything from the fractions. When silver reaches two hundred dirhams, take five dirhams from it. And whatever exceeds, take nothing from it until it reaches forty dirhams. And when it reaches forty dirhams, take one dirham. (B) From 'Ata it is narrated that if a man takes out the zakat of his wealth and it is lost, it suffices for him.

[PAGE 321]
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part One, Book of Zakat
If a man is the owner of nisab but the year has not passed over this nisab, and he wants to give zakat immediately, it is permissible. The zakat will be discharged. The nisab wealth is the fundamental cause, and it exists, so the cause exists, therefore the payment of zakat is valid. (2) In a hadith from 'Ali: 'That al-'Abbas asked the Prophet about advancing sadaqah before it becomes due, and he permitted him to do so.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Advancing Zakat, p. 236, no. 624; Tirmidhi, Chapter on Advancing Zakat, p. 146, no. 678) From this hadith it is known that he can give zakat before the year passes because the Prophet permitted al-'Abbas.

Marginal note: (A) Al-'Abbas asked the Prophet about giving zakat early before the time, and he granted permission for that.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi ruling that it is permissible to give zakat before the completion of the lunar year, provided one already owns the nisab. The rationale is that the nisab itself is the cause (sabab) for zakat; since the cause is present, the payment is valid even before the year ends. Two proofs are cited: first, the instruction to Mu'adh regarding the nisab thresholds for silver, which implies that zakat can be assessed on existing wealth; second, and more directly, the hadith of al-'Abbas who asked the Prophet about advancing zakat and was granted permission. The commentary notes that this permission is a concession (rukhsah). The Hanafi school thus allows ta'jil al-zakah (advancing zakat) as long as the nisab is in one's possession. This is distinguished from the view of some scholars who may require the year to pass. The practical benefit: one can pay zakat early to help a needy person sooner without waiting for the year to end.

Key Terms
تعجيل الزكاة (ta'jil al-zakah): Paying zakat before the completion of the lunar year.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum wealth threshold triggering zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, paying zakat before the year is valid because the nisab triggers the obligation, and the Prophet explicitly permitted it.
